GPT-4o on 7.NS.A.3-fraction

Common Core Standard 7.NS.A.3-fraction

This standard covers the following:

Solve real-world and mathematical problems involving the four operations with rational numbers.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Carla has a garden and wants to calculate the amount of cucumbers she will be able to grow. She noticed that the number of cucumbers she could grow per plant was determined by multiplying 22/3 by 22/19. After a few months, she realized that she could grow her production by multiplying the initial amount by 23/17. How many cucumbers is she expecting to grow per plant after adjusting her production method?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the number of cucumbers Carla can grow per plant, we need to follow the steps given in the problem.

First, we calculate the initial number of cucumbers per plant by multiplying \( \frac{22}{3} \) by \( \frac{22}{19} \):

\[
\frac{22}{3} \times \frac{22}{19} = \frac{22 \times 22}{3 \times 19} = \frac{484}{57}
\]

Next, Carla increases her production by multiplying the initial amount by \( \frac{23}{17} \):

\[
\frac{484}{57} \times \frac{23}{17} = \frac{484 \times 23}{57 \times 17}
\]

We now perform the multiplications in the numerator and the denominator:

\[
484 \times 23 = 11132
\]
\[
57 \times 17 = 969
\]

Thus, the number of cucumbers per plant after adjusting her production method is:

\[
\frac{11132}{969}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 11132 and 969. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

\[
11132 \div 969 \approx 11.49 \quad \text{(remainder 493)}
\]
\[
969 \div 493 \approx 1.97 \quad \text{(remainder 476)}
\]
\[
493 \div 476 \approx 1.03 \quad \text{(remainder 17)}
\]
\[
476 \div 17 = 28 \quad \text{(remainder 0)}
\]

The GCD is 17. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 17:

\[
\frac{11132 \div 17}{969 \div 17} = \frac{655}{57}
\]

Therefore, the number of cucumbers Carla is expecting to grow per plant after adjusting her production method is:

### Answer: \(\frac{655}{57}\)

Expected answer: 11132/969

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Pierre has 19/4 kg of grapes. One afternoon, he ate 7/25 kg of them. In the evening, his mother gave him 30/9 kg more grapes. How many kilograms of grapes does Pierre have now?

GPT-4o: 

To determine how many kilograms of grapes Pierre has now, we need to perform the following steps:

1. Subtract the amount of grapes Pierre ate from the initial amount he had.
2. Add the amount of grapes his mother gave him to the remaining amount.

First, let's convert all fractions to have a common denominator where necessary.

Initial amount of grapes: \( \frac{19}{4} \)

Amount of grapes Pierre ate: \( \frac{7}{25} \)

To subtract \( \frac{7}{25} \) from \( \frac{19}{4} \), we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 4 and 25 is 100.

Convert \( \frac{19}{4} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 100:
\[ \frac{19}{4} = \frac{19 \times 25}{4 \times 25} = \frac{475}{100} \]

Convert \( \frac{7}{25} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 100:
\[ \frac{7}{25} = \frac{7 \times 4}{25 \times 4} = \frac{28}{100} \]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[ \frac{475}{100} - \frac{28}{100} = \frac{475 - 28}{100} = \frac{447}{100} \]

Next, we add the amount of grapes his mother gave him: \( \frac{30}{9} \)

Convert \( \frac{30}{9} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 100:
\[ \frac{30}{9} = \frac{30 \times 11.1111}{9 \times 11.1111} = \frac{333.3333}{100} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{447}{100} + \frac{333.3333}{100} = \frac{780.3333}{100} \]

Simplify the fraction:
\[ \frac{780.3333}{100} = 7.803333 \]

### Answer: 7.803333 kg

Expected answer: 2341/300

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: King Arthur is calculating the costs for restoring his castle. The wall repairs cost 26/22 of his castle's annual budget. Meanwhile, the moat renovations cost an additional 4/29 of the budget. Finally, installing new defensive catapults takes up an 11/3 portion of the budget. How much (expressed as a fraction of the castle's annual budget) has King Arthur spent on these projects in total?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total fraction of the castle's annual budget that King Arthur has spent on these projects, we need to add the fractions representing each project's cost.

The fractions are:
- Wall repairs: \( \frac{26}{22} \)
- Moat renovations: \( \frac{4}{29} \)
- Defensive catapults: \( \frac{11}{3} \)

First, simplify the fraction for the wall repairs:
\[ \frac{26}{22} = \frac{13}{11} \]

Now, we need to find a common denominator to add these fractions. The denominators are 11, 29, and 3. The least common multiple (LCM) of these numbers is 957.

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 957:
\[ \frac{13}{11} = \frac{13 \times 87}{11 \times 87} = \frac{1131}{957} \]
\[ \frac{4}{29} = \frac{4 \times 33}{29 \times 33} = \frac{132}{957} \]
\[ \frac{11}{3} = \frac{11 \times 319}{3 \times 319} = \frac{3509}{957} \]

Now, add these fractions:
\[ \frac{1131}{957} + \frac{132}{957} + \frac{3509}{957} = \frac{1131 + 132 + 3509}{957} = \frac{4772}{957} \]

Simplify the resulting fraction:
\[ \frac{4772}{957} = \frac{4772 \div 239}{957 \div 239} = \frac{20}{4} = 5 \]

### Answer: 5

Expected answer: 4772/957

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: A giraffe at the local zoo has a peculiar eating habit. When it is fed 25/19 lbs of acacia leaves, it eats 30/26 times more than what it usually does in a day. If the zoo calculates the weekly feeding amount by multiplying the daily intake by itself (making the result "weekly feeding amount squared") and then multiplying that with the regular daily intake, how many pounds of acacia leaves should they prepare for the giraffe for a week? Calculate ((25 / 19) * (30 / 26))^2 * ((25 / 19) * (30 / 26)) and provide your answer.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Calculate the daily intake of acacia leaves.
2. Square the daily intake to get the weekly feeding amount squared.
3. Multiply the weekly feeding amount squared by the daily intake to get the total weekly feeding amount.

First, let's calculate the daily intake:
\[
\text{Daily intake} = \left(\frac{25}{19}\right) \times \left(\frac{30}{26}\right)
\]

We can simplify this multiplication:
\[
\text{Daily intake} = \frac{25 \times 30}{19 \times 26} = \frac{750}{494}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{750}{494}\):
\[
\frac{750}{494} = \frac{375}{247} \quad \text{(dividing both numerator and denominator by 2)}
\]

Now, we square the daily intake to get the weekly feeding amount squared:
\[
\left(\frac{375}{247}\right)^2 = \frac{375^2}{247^2} = \frac{140625}{61009}
\]

Finally, we multiply the weekly feeding amount squared by the daily intake:
\[
\left(\frac{375}{247}\right)^2 \times \frac{375}{247} = \frac{140625}{61009} \times \frac{375}{247} = \frac{140625 \times 375}{61009 \times 247}
\]

Calculating the numerator and the denominator:
\[
140625 \times 375 = 52734375
\]
\[
61009 \times 247 = 15069223
\]

Thus, the total weekly feeding amount is:
\[
\frac{52734375}{15069223}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{52734375}{15069223}\) lbs

Expected answer: 52734375/15069223

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Continuing from the previous scenario, the zookeepers found an additional giraffe with the same peculiar eating habits. They decided to combine the weekly feeding amounts for both giraffes. If the feeding amount for each giraffe for the week is calculated as in the previous problem ((25 / 19) * (30 / 26))^2 * ((25 / 19) * (30 / 26)), what would be the total amount of acacia leaves the zoo should prepare to feed both giraffes for a week? Calculate (y + y) where y is the weekly feeding amount for one giraffe.

GPT-4o: 

To find the total amount of acacia leaves needed to feed both giraffes for a week, we need to double the weekly feeding amount calculated for one giraffe.

From the previous problem, we determined that the weekly feeding amount for one giraffe is:
\[
\frac{52734375}{15069223} \text{ lbs}
\]

Since there are two giraffes, we need to calculate:
\[
2 \times \frac{52734375}{15069223}
\]

This can be written as:
\[
\frac{2 \times 52734375}{15069223} = \frac{105468750}{15069223}
\]

Thus, the total amount of acacia leaves needed to feed both giraffes for a week is:
\[
\frac{105468750}{15069223} \text{ lbs}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{105468750}{15069223}\) lbs

Expected answer: 105468750/15069223

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: In continuation of the old scenario, now imagine that the same giraffe's diet has changed slightly. Instead of eating 30/26 times more than its usual intake, it now eats 27/26 times more. So now, with these changes, how much acacia leaves should the zookeepers prepare for a week? Calculate ((25 / 19) * (27 / 26))^2 * ((25 / 19) * (27 / 26)) to estimate the total amount of food needed.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow similar steps as before but with the updated multiplier.

1. Calculate the new daily intake of acacia leaves.
2. Square the daily intake to get the weekly feeding amount squared.
3. Multiply the weekly feeding amount squared by the daily intake to get the total weekly feeding amount.

First, let's calculate the new daily intake:
\[
\text{Daily intake} = \left(\frac{25}{19}\right) \times \left(\frac{27}{26}\right)
\]

We can simplify this multiplication:
\[
\text{Daily intake} = \frac{25 \times 27}{19 \times 26} = \frac{675}{494}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{675}{494}\):
\[
\frac{675}{494} = \frac{225}{164} \quad \text{(dividing both numerator and denominator by 3)}
\]

Now, we square the daily intake to get the weekly feeding amount squared:
\[
\left(\frac{225}{164}\right)^2 = \frac{225^2}{164^2} = \frac{50625}{26896}
\]

Finally, we multiply the weekly feeding amount squared by the daily intake:
\[
\left(\frac{225}{164}\right)^2 \times \frac{225}{164} = \frac{50625}{26896} \times \frac{225}{164} = \frac{50625 \times 225}{26896 \times 164}
\]

Calculating the numerator and the denominator:
\[
50625 \times 225 = 11390625
\]
\[
26896 \times 164 = 4410944
\]

Thus, the total weekly feeding amount is:
\[
\frac{11390625}{4410944}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{11390625}{4410944}\) lbs

Expected answer: 307546875/120553784

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Lara wants to make a necklace. The necklace requires (11/3) feet of yarn. She also wants to add smaller beads which will extend the length of the necklace by (8/30) feet. How many feet of materials will Lara need to make the necklace?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total length of materials Lara will need, we need to add the length of the yarn and the length added by the beads.

First, let's convert both fractions to have a common denominator to make the addition easier. The denominators are 3 and 30. The least common multiple of 3 and 30 is 30.

Convert \(\frac{11}{3}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 30:
\[
\frac{11}{3} = \frac{11 \times 10}{3 \times 10} = \frac{110}{30}
\]

Now, we can add \(\frac{110}{30}\) and \(\frac{8}{30}\):
\[
\frac{110}{30} + \frac{8}{30} = \frac{110 + 8}{30} = \frac{118}{30}
\]

We can simplify \(\frac{118}{30}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
\[
\frac{118 \div 2}{30 \div 2} = \frac{59}{15}
\]

Thus, the total length of materials Lara will need is \(\frac{59}{15}\) feet.

### Answer: \(\frac{59}{15}\) feet

Expected answer: 59/15

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Lara was pleased with her initial necklace design, but she decided she wants to add some larger beads to the necklace. These larger beads require an additional (24/17) feet of yarn. How many total feet of material will Lara now need to finish her necklace with the added beads?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total length of materials Lara will need with the added larger beads, we need to add the previous total length of materials to the length required for the larger beads.

From the previous calculation, the total length of materials without the larger beads is \(\frac{59}{15}\) feet. The additional length required for the larger beads is \(\frac{24}{17}\) feet.

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The denominators are 15 and 17. The least common multiple of 15 and 17 is 255.

Convert \(\frac{59}{15}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 255:
\[
\frac{59}{15} = \frac{59 \times 17}{15 \times 17} = \frac{1003}{255}
\]

Convert \(\frac{24}{17}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 255:
\[
\frac{24}{17} = \frac{24 \times 15}{17 \times 15} = \frac{360}{255}
\]

Now, we can add \(\frac{1003}{255}\) and \(\frac{360}{255}\):
\[
\frac{1003}{255} + \frac{360}{255} = \frac{1003 + 360}{255} = \frac{1363}{255}
\]

Thus, the total length of materials Lara will need with the added larger beads is \(\frac{1363}{255}\) feet.

### Answer: \(\frac{1363}{255}\) feet

Expected answer: 1363/255

Correct? Yes

Problem: Lara realized that she made a slight miscalculation. The amount of smaller beads she wants to add to the necklace extends its length by (8/28) feet not by (8/30) feet as she initially thought. Given this new information, how many total feet of material will Lara need to make her necklace, before adding the larger beads?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total length of materials Lara will need with the corrected length of the smaller beads, we need to add the length of the yarn and the corrected length added by the beads.

First, let's convert both fractions to have a common denominator to make the addition easier. The denominators are 3 and 28. The least common multiple of 3 and 28 is 84.

Convert \(\frac{11}{3}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 84:
\[
\frac{11}{3} = \frac{11 \times 28}{3 \times 28} = \frac{308}{84}
\]

Convert \(\frac{8}{28}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 84:
\[
\frac{8}{28} = \frac{8 \times 3}{28 \times 3} = \frac{24}{84}
\]

Now, we can add \(\frac{308}{84}\) and \(\frac{24}{84}\):
\[
\frac{308}{84} + \frac{24}{84} = \frac{308 + 24}{84} = \frac{332}{84}
\]

We can simplify \(\frac{332}{84}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 4:
\[
\frac{332 \div 4}{84 \div 4} = \frac{83}{21}
\]

Thus, the total length of materials Lara will need is \(\frac{83}{21}\) feet.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Two planes depart from an airport at the exact same time. Plane A is flying at a speed of 24/11 miles per minute and Plane B is flying at a speed of 26/27 miles per minute. How much farther (in miles) did Plane A travel than Plane B after exactly one minute, assuming they keep flying at a stable speed? Calculate the difference and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much farther Plane A traveled than Plane B after exactly one minute, we need to calculate the distance each plane traveled in that time and then find the difference.

First, let's calculate the distance traveled by Plane A in one minute:
\[ \text{Distance traveled by Plane A} = \frac{24}{11} \text{ miles per minute} \times 1 \text{ minute} = \frac{24}{11} \text{ miles} \]

Next, let's calculate the distance traveled by Plane B in one minute:
\[ \text{Distance traveled by Plane B} = \frac{26}{27} \text{ miles per minute} \times 1 \text{ minute} = \frac{26}{27} \text{ miles} \]

Now, we need to find the difference between the distances traveled by Plane A and Plane B:
\[ \text{Difference} = \frac{24}{11} - \frac{26}{27} \]

To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 11 and 27 is 297. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{24}{11} = \frac{24 \times 27}{11 \times 27} = \frac{648}{297} \]
\[ \frac{26}{27} = \frac{26 \times 11}{27 \times 11} = \frac{286}{297} \]

Now, subtract the fractions:
\[ \frac{648}{297} - \frac{286}{297} = \frac{648 - 286}{297} = \frac{362}{297} \]

The fraction \(\frac{362}{297}\) can be simplified by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 362 and 297. The GCD of 362 and 297 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{362}{297}\)

Expected answer: 362/297

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Following on from the previous problem: Let's say Plane A has slowed down slightly and is now flying at a speed of 24/11 miles per minute. Meanwhile, Plane B has also adjusted its speed and is now flying at 2/27 miles per minute. How much farther (in miles) did Plane A travel than Plane B after exactly one minute, assuming they keep flying at the new speeds? Calculate the difference and write your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much farther Plane A traveled than Plane B after exactly one minute at their new speeds, we need to calculate the distance each plane traveled in that time and then find the difference.

First, let's calculate the distance traveled by Plane A in one minute:
\[ \text{Distance traveled by Plane A} = \frac{24}{11} \text{ miles per minute} \times 1 \text{ minute} = \frac{24}{11} \text{ miles} \]

Next, let's calculate the distance traveled by Plane B in one minute:
\[ \text{Distance traveled by Plane B} = \frac{2}{27} \text{ miles per minute} \times 1 \text{ minute} = \frac{2}{27} \text{ miles} \]

Now, we need to find the difference between the distances traveled by Plane A and Plane B:
\[ \text{Difference} = \frac{24}{11} - \frac{2}{27} \]

To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 11 and 27 is 297. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{24}{11} = \frac{24 \times 27}{11 \times 27} = \frac{648}{297} \]
\[ \frac{2}{27} = \frac{2 \times 11}{27 \times 11} = \frac{22}{297} \]

Now, subtract the fractions:
\[ \frac{648}{297} - \frac{22}{297} = \frac{648 - 22}{297} = \frac{626}{297} \]

The fraction \(\frac{626}{297}\) can be simplified by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 626 and 297. The GCD of 626 and 297 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{626}{297}\)

Expected answer: 626/297

Correct? Yes

Problem: In the wild, an adult bear eats about 14/7 pounds of fish per day. A young bear eats about 25/13 pounds of fish per day. Calculate the combined amount that both bears eat per day by multiplying 14/7 by 25/13.

GPT-4o: 

To find the combined amount of fish that both bears eat per day, we need to multiply the fractions representing the amount of fish each bear eats.

First, let's simplify the fraction for the adult bear:
\[ \frac{14}{7} = 2 \]

Next, we multiply this by the fraction for the young bear:
\[ 2 \times \frac{25}{13} \]

To perform this multiplication, we multiply the numerators and the denominators:
\[ 2 \times \frac{25}{13} = \frac{2 \times 25}{1 \times 13} = \frac{50}{13} \]

So, the combined amount of fish that both bears eat per day is:
\[ \frac{50}{13} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{50}{13}\)

Expected answer: 50/13

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Toby plays guitar. His first song takes 12/8 hours to play and his second song takes 12/3 hours to play. How long does it take Toby to play both of his songs? Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's simplify the time it takes Toby to play each song.

For the first song:
\[ \frac{12}{8} = \frac{12 \div 4}{8 \div 4} = \frac{3}{2} \text{ hours} \]

For the second song:
\[ \frac{12}{3} = 4 \text{ hours} \]

Now, we add the times together:
\[ \frac{3}{2} + 4 \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 2 and 1 (since 4 can be written as \(\frac{4}{1}\)) is 2.

Convert 4 to a fraction with a denominator of 2:
\[ 4 = \frac{4 \times 2}{1 \times 2} = \frac{8}{2} \]

Now add the fractions:
\[ \frac{3}{2} + \frac{8}{2} = \frac{3 + 8}{2} = \frac{11}{2} \]

So, it takes Toby \(\frac{11}{2}\) hours to play both of his songs.

### Answer: \(\frac{11}{2}\)

Expected answer: 11/2

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After playing his two songs, Toby decides to play a third song that takes 19/14 hours. How long does it take Toby to play all three songs? Write your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

First, we know the total time Toby takes to play his first two songs is \(\frac{11}{2}\) hours.

Now, we need to add the time for the third song, which is \(\frac{19}{14}\) hours.

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 2 and 14 is 14.

Convert \(\frac{11}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 14:
\[ \frac{11}{2} = \frac{11 \times 7}{2 \times 7} = \frac{77}{14} \]

Now add the fractions:
\[ \frac{77}{14} + \frac{19}{14} = \frac{77 + 19}{14} = \frac{96}{14} \]

Simplify the fraction by dividing the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
\[ \frac{96 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{48}{7} \]

So, it takes Toby \(\frac{48}{7}\) hours to play all three songs.

### Answer: \(\frac{48}{7}\)

Expected answer: 48/7

Correct? Yes

First, let's simplify the time it takes Toby to play each song.

For the first song:

Now add the fractions:

So, it takes Toby \(\frac{24}{5}\) hours to play both of his songs.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Suppose you have 28 out of 29 chocolate bars. Then, you found 8 out of 22 more chocolate bars. What fraction represents the total chocolate bars you have now?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine the total number of chocolate bars you have.

You initially have 28 out of 29 chocolate bars. This can be written as:
\[ \frac{28}{29} \]

Next, you found 8 out of 22 more chocolate bars. This can be written as:
\[ \frac{8}{22} \]

To find the total number of chocolate bars, we need to add these two fractions. First, we simplify the second fraction:
\[ \frac{8}{22} = \frac{4}{11} \]

Now, we need a common denominator to add these fractions. The least common multiple of 29 and 11 is 319. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{28}{29} = \frac{28 \times 11}{29 \times 11} = \frac{308}{319} \]
\[ \frac{4}{11} = \frac{4 \times 29}{11 \times 29} = \frac{116}{319} \]

Now, we add the fractions:
\[ \frac{308}{319} + \frac{116}{319} = \frac{308 + 116}{319} = \frac{424}{319} \]

So, the fraction representing the total chocolate bars you have now is:
\[ \frac{424}{319} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{424}{319}\)

Expected answer: 424/319

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: A compass maker is creating some specialty compasses. The compass needle is made from a special material. It takes 27/26 of a pound to create one needle. If the maker is trying to produce two identical needles, how much material will he require? After producing the two needles, the maker realizes he needs to produce an additional piece for the compass that requires 27/6 pounds of the material. How much total material will the compass maker need to produce the two needles and the additional piece?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine the amount of material needed to produce two identical needles. Each needle requires \( \frac{27}{26} \) pounds of material.

For two needles:
\[
2 \times \frac{27}{26} = \frac{54}{26} = \frac{27}{13} \text{ pounds}
\]

Next, the additional piece requires \( \frac{27}{6} \) pounds of material.

Now, we need to find the total material required for both the needles and the additional piece:
\[
\frac{27}{13} + \frac{27}{6}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 13 and 6 is 78.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 78:
\[
\frac{27}{13} = \frac{27 \times 6}{13 \times 6} = \frac{162}{78}
\]
\[
\frac{27}{6} = \frac{27 \times 13}{6 \times 13} = \frac{351}{78}
\]

\[

\]

Simplify the fraction:
\[
\frac{513}{78} = \frac{513 \div 3}{78 \div 3} = \frac{171}{26}
\]

Thus, the total material required is:
\[
\frac{171}{26} \text{ pounds}

For the first candle:
\[ \frac{6}{4} \]

\[ \frac{6 \div 2}{4 \div 2} = \frac{3}{2} \]

For the second candle:
\[ \frac{14}{16} \]
We can simplify this fraction by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
\[ \frac{14 \div 2}{16 \div 2} = \frac{7}{8} \]

Now, we need to find the total rate at which the two candles burn together. To do this, we add the two simplified rates:
\[ \frac{3}{2} + \frac{7}{8} \]

\[ \frac{3}{2} = \frac{3 \times 4}{2 \times 4} = \frac{12}{8} \]

Now we can add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{12}{8} + \frac{7}{8} = \frac{12 + 7}{8} = \frac{19}{8} \]

So, the total rate at which the two candles burn together is:
\[ \frac{19}{8} \] inches per hour.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Imagine you're a music producer who is working on a new song. Your resources are divided into different sections. - First, you dedicate 16/4 hours to composing the music and another 16/29 hours to writing the lyrics. This is your initial time investment for the song (let's call it p). - Then, you spend 28/13 hours for mixing and mastering the song in addition to the initial time investment (let's call this new total time b). - Suddenly, a drummer you hired for a session uses 18/4 hours less because he finished his parts quickly. What is the final time you spent on producing the song, if your total time is expressed as (b - (18 / 4))?

GPT-4o: 

Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. **Initial Time Investment (p):**
   - Time spent composing the music: \( \frac{16}{4} \) hours
   - Time spent writing the lyrics: \( \frac{16}{29} \) hours

   Calculate the total initial time investment \( p \):
   \[
   p = \frac{16}{4} + \frac{16}{29}
   \]

   Simplify \( \frac{16}{4} \):
   \[
   \frac{16}{4} = 4
   \]

   So,
   \[
   p = 4 + \frac{16}{29}
   \]

2. **Total Time Including Mixing and Mastering (b):**
   - Additional time for mixing and mastering: \( \frac{28}{13} \) hours

   Calculate the new total time \( b \):
   \[
   b = p + \frac{28}{13}
   \]

   Substitute \( p \) into the equation:
   \[
   b = 4 + \frac{16}{29} + \frac{28}{13}
   \]

3. **Final Time After Drummer's Adjustment:**
   - Drummer's time reduction: \( \frac{18}{4} \) hours

   Calculate the final time:
   \[
   \text{Final Time} = b - \frac{18}{4}
   \]

   Substitute \( b \) into the equation:
   \[
   \text{Final Time} = \left( 4 + \frac{16}{29} + \frac{28}{13} \right) - \frac{18}{4}
   \]

4. **Simplify the Expression:**
   - Convert all fractions to a common denominator if necessary.

   First, find a common denominator for \( \frac{16}{29} \) and \( \frac{28}{13} \):
   \[
   \text{Common denominator} = 29 \times 13 = 377
   \]

   Convert \( \frac{16}{29} \) and \( \frac{28}{13} \) to have the common denominator:
   \[
   \frac{16}{29} = \frac{16 \times 13}{29 \times 13} = \frac{208}{377}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{28}{13} = \frac{28 \times 29}{13 \times 29} = \frac{812}{377}
   \]

   Combine the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{208}{377} + \frac{812}{377} = \frac{208 + 812}{377} = \frac{1020}{377}
   \]

   So,
   \[
   b = 4 + \frac{1020}{377}
   \]

   Now, convert \( 4 \) to a fraction with the same denominator:
   \[
   4 = \frac{4 \times 377}{377} = \frac{1508}{377}
   \]

   Combine:
   \[
   b = \frac{1508}{377} + \frac{1020}{377} = \frac{2528}{377}
   \]

   Now, subtract the drummer's time:
   \[
   \frac{18}{4} = 4.5
   \]

   Convert \( 4.5 \) to a fraction with the same denominator:
   \[
   4.5 = \frac{4.5 \times 377}{377} = \frac{1696.5}{377}
   \]

   Subtract:
   \[
   \text{Final Time} = \frac{2528}{377} - \frac{1696.5}{377} = \frac{831.5}{377}
   \]

   Simplify the fraction if possible:
   \[
   \frac{831.5}{377} = 2.205
   \]

### Answer: 2.205 hours

Expected answer: 1663/754

Correct? No

Problem: Monica has 21/15 dozens of cookies at her bakery shop. Later in the day, she bakes additional 29/17 dozens of cookies to add into her stock. At the end of the day, she decides to increase her total stock of cookies by a ratio of 7/5 for an upcoming cookie festival. How many dozens of cookies will Monica have for the cookie festival?

GPT-4o: 

First, we need to find the total number of dozens of cookies Monica has before increasing her stock. We start by adding the two fractions:

\[
\frac{21}{15} + \frac{29}{17}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 15 and 17 is 255. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[
\frac{21}{15} = \frac{21 \times 17}{15 \times 17} = \frac{357}{255}
\]

\[
\frac{29}{17} = \frac{29 \times 15}{17 \times 15} = \frac{435}{255}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{357}{255} + \frac{435}{255} = \frac{357 + 435}{255} = \frac{792}{255}
\]

Next, we simplify the fraction \(\frac{792}{255}\). We find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 792 and 255, which is 3:

\[
\frac{792 \div 3}{255 \div 3} = \frac{264}{85}
\]

So, Monica has \(\frac{264}{85}\) dozens of cookies before increasing her stock. Now, she decides to increase her total stock by a ratio of \(\frac{7}{5}\):

\[
\frac{264}{85} \times \frac{7}{5} = \frac{264 \times 7}{85 \times 5} = \frac{1848}{425}
\]

We simplify the fraction \(\frac{1848}{425}\). The GCD of 1848 and 425 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

Thus, Monica will have \(\frac{1848}{425}\) dozens of cookies for the cookie festival.

### Answer: \(\frac{1848}{425}\) dozens

Expected answer: 1848/425

Correct? Yes

Problem: In a bakery, a certain cake recipe requires 26/24 kg of sugar per cake. If a chef starts with 28 kg of sugar, how many kilograms of sugar will they have left after making one cake and then adding 10/6 kg of sugar to their supply?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine how much sugar is used to make one cake. The recipe requires \( \frac{26}{24} \) kg of sugar per cake. We can simplify this fraction:

\[
\frac{26}{24} = \frac{13}{12} \text{ kg}
\]

Next, the chef starts with 28 kg of sugar. After making one cake, the amount of sugar left is:

\[
28 - \frac{13}{12}
\]

To subtract these, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 28 and \( \frac{13}{12} \) is 12. We convert 28 to a fraction with a denominator of 12:

\[
28 = \frac{28 \times 12}{12} = \frac{336}{12}
\]

Now, we subtract \( \frac{13}{12} \) from \( \frac{336}{12} \):

\[
\frac{336}{12} - \frac{13}{12} = \frac{336 - 13}{12} = \frac{323}{12}
\]

Next, the chef adds \( \frac{10}{6} \) kg of sugar to their supply. We simplify \( \frac{10}{6} \):

\[
\frac{10}{6} = \frac{5}{3}
\]

We need a common denominator to add \( \frac{323}{12} \) and \( \frac{5}{3} \). The common denominator for 12 and 3 is 12. We convert \( \frac{5}{3} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 12:

\[
\frac{5}{3} = \frac{5 \times 4}{3 \times 4} = \frac{20}{12}
\]

Now, we add \( \frac{323}{12} \) and \( \frac{20}{12} \):

\[
\frac{323}{12} + \frac{20}{12} = \frac{323 + 20}{12} = \frac{343}{12}
\]

Finally, we simplify \( \frac{343}{12} \):

\[
\frac{343}{12} \approx 28.5833 \text{ kg}
\]

### Answer: \( \frac{343}{12} \) kg or approximately 28.5833 kg

Expected answer: 343/12

Correct? Yes

Problem: Princess Lily was dining at a finely set table and in front of her, two dishes were placed, one with slices of apple pie and the other with slices of blueberry pie. She can eat pie slices endlessly! She ate 10 out of the 12 slices of the apple pie and 10 out of the 29 slices of the blueberry pie. How much of the pies (combined) did she eat? Represent your answer as a fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much of the pies Princess Lily ate, we need to add the fractions of each pie she consumed.

First, let's calculate the fraction of the apple pie she ate:
\[ \text{Fraction of apple pie eaten} = \frac{10}{12} \]

Next, let's calculate the fraction of the blueberry pie she ate:
\[ \text{Fraction of blueberry pie eaten} = \frac{10}{29} \]

To find the total amount of pie she ate, we need to add these two fractions:
\[ \frac{10}{12} + \frac{10}{29} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 12 and 29 is 348. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

\[ \frac{10}{12} = \frac{10 \times 29}{12 \times 29} = \frac{290}{348} \]
\[ \frac{10}{29} = \frac{10 \times 12}{29 \times 12} = \frac{120}{348} \]

Now, we add the fractions:
\[ \frac{290}{348} + \frac{120}{348} = \frac{290 + 120}{348} = \frac{410}{348} \]

This fraction can be simplified by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor (GCD). The GCD of 410 and 348 is 2:

\[ \frac{410 \div 2}{348 \div 2} = \frac{205}{174} \]

Thus, the fraction representing the total amount of pie Princess Lily ate is:
\[ \frac{205}{174} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{205}{174}\)

Expected answer: 205/174

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: As Princess Lily was about to leave the dining room, she noticed another plate - this one filled with 29 slices of peach pie. She decided to help herself and ate 10 of the slices. Before her peach pie adventure, she had already eaten an entire 10-slice chocolate cake. Now, how much of the total food (chocolate cake and peach pie) did Princess Lily eat? Please represent your answer as a fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much of the total food Princess Lily ate, we need to consider both the chocolate cake and the peach pie.

First, let's calculate the fraction of the peach pie she ate:
\[ \text{Fraction of peach pie eaten} = \frac{10}{29} \]

Next, let's consider the chocolate cake. Since she ate the entire 10-slice chocolate cake, the fraction of the chocolate cake she ate is:
\[ \text{Fraction of chocolate cake eaten} = \frac{10}{10} = 1 \]

Now, we need to add these two fractions to find the total amount of food she ate:
\[ 1 + \frac{10}{29} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 1 and \(\frac{10}{29}\) is 29. We convert the whole number 1 to a fraction with this common denominator:
\[ 1 = \frac{29}{29} \]

\[ \frac{29}{29} + \frac{10}{29} = \frac{29 + 10}{29} = \frac{39}{29} \]

Problem: A police investigator is analyzing two evidence specimens. The first specimen has a unique property that decreases its value by 26 out of every 6 units. The second specimen decreases its value by 25 out of every 17 units. The investigator needs to find the ratio of these changes, referred to as indicator i. Additionally, he needs to figure out a set of changes in another pair of evidence specimens. The first one of this pair increases its value by 18 out of every 8 units and the second one increases its value by 17 out of every 23 units. The investigator has to find the difference between these two rates and refer to it as indicator h. He then combines these two indicators (h and i) by multiplying them to get a final evidence factor, referred to as indicator f. This will help determine the likelihood of a particular suspectâ€™s involvement. Calculate the value of f.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to calculate the indicators \( i \) and \( h \) and then multiply them to find the final evidence factor \( f \).

First, let's calculate indicator \( i \):

1. The first specimen decreases its value by 26 out of every 6 units. This can be expressed as a ratio:
   \[
   \frac{26}{6}
   \]

2. The second specimen decreases its value by 25 out of every 17 units. This can be expressed as a ratio:
   \[
   \frac{25}{17}
   \]

3. The ratio of these changes (indicator \( i \)) is:
   \[
   i = \frac{\frac{26}{6}}{\frac{25}{17}} = \frac{26}{6} \times \frac{17}{25} = \frac{26 \times 17}{6 \times 25} = \frac{442}{150}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{442}{150} = \frac{221}{75}
   \]

Next, let's calculate indicator \( h \):

1. The first specimen increases its value by 18 out of every 8 units. This can be expressed as a ratio:
   \[
   \frac{18}{8}
   \]

2. The second specimen increases its value by 17 out of every 23 units. This can be expressed as a ratio:
   \[
   \frac{17}{23}
   \]

3. The difference between these two rates (indicator \( h \)) is:
   \[
   h = \frac{18}{8} - \frac{17}{23}
   \]

4. To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 8 and 23 is 184:
   \[
   \frac{18}{8} = \frac{18 \times 23}{8 \times 23} = \frac{414}{184}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{17}{23} = \frac{17 \times 8}{23 \times 8} = \frac{136}{184}
   \]

5. Subtract the fractions:
   \[
   h = \frac{414}{184} - \frac{136}{184} = \frac{278}{184}
   \]

6. Simplify the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{278}{184} = \frac{139}{92}
   \]

Finally, we combine these two indicators by multiplying them to get the final evidence factor \( f \):

1. Multiply \( i \) and \( h \):
   \[
   f = \frac{221}{75} \times \frac{139}{92} = \frac{221 \times 139}{75 \times 92} = \frac{30719}{6900}
   \]

2. Simplify the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{30719}{6900}
   \]

Since 30719 and 6900 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{30719}{6900}\)

Expected answer: 30719/6900

Correct? Yes

Problem: In a wildlife park, there are lions and giraffes. During one particular year, the gestation period of a lioness is represented as 20/22 of a year, while a giraffe's gestation period is 15 years. Find the total gestation period of both animals together. Later in the same year, a lioness is pregnant again but this time her gestation period reduces by 15/20 of a year compared to the earlier total gestation period of both animals. How long will it take for the lioness to give birth this second time?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's find the total gestation period of both animals together.

1. The gestation period of a lioness is given as \( \frac{20}{22} \) of a year.
2. The gestation period of a giraffe is given as 15 years.

To find the total gestation period, we add these two periods together:
\[ \text{Total gestation period} = \frac{20}{22} + 15 \]

Simplify \( \frac{20}{22} \):
\[ \frac{20}{22} = \frac{10}{11} \]

So, the total gestation period is:
\[ \frac{10}{11} + 15 \]

Next, we need to find the reduced gestation period for the lioness in the second instance. The reduction is given as \( \frac{15}{20} \) of a year.

Simplify \( \frac{15}{20} \):
\[ \frac{15}{20} = \frac{3}{4} \]

Now, subtract this reduction from the total gestation period of both animals:
\[ \text{Reduced gestation period} = \left( \frac{10}{11} + 15 \right) - \frac{3}{4} \]

First, convert \( 15 \) to a fraction with a common denominator with \( \frac{10}{11} \):
\[ 15 = \frac{165}{11} \]

So, the total gestation period in terms of a common denominator is:
\[ \frac{10}{11} + \frac{165}{11} = \frac{175}{11} \]

Now, convert \( \frac{3}{4} \) to a fraction with a common denominator with \( \frac{175}{11} \):
\[ \frac{3}{4} = \frac{3 \times 11}{4 \times 11} = \frac{33}{44} \]

Convert \( \frac{175}{11} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 44:
\[ \frac{175}{11} = \frac{175 \times 4}{11 \times 4} = \frac{700}{44} \]

Subtract \( \frac{33}{44} \) from \( \frac{700}{44} \):
\[ \frac{700}{44} - \frac{33}{44} = \frac{700 - 33}{44} = \frac{667}{44} \]

Simplify \( \frac{667}{44} \):
\[ \frac{667}{44} = 15.159 \]

So, the reduced gestation period for the lioness is approximately 15.159 years.

### Answer: 15.159 years

Expected answer: 667/44

Correct? No

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: A rectangle's length is 30/7 meters and its width is 19/6 meters. The area of the rectangle is found by multiplying the length and the width. If a similar rectangle has an area which is 18/17 times bigger than the original rectangle, what is the area of the similar rectangle?

GPT-4o: 

First, we need to find the area of the original rectangle. The area \( A \) of a rectangle is given by the formula:

\[ A = \text{length} \times \text{width} \]

Given the length is \( \frac{30}{7} \) meters and the width is \( \frac{19}{6} \) meters, we can calculate the area as follows:

\[ A = \frac{30}{7} \times \frac{19}{6} \]

To multiply these fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[ A = \frac{30 \times 19}{7 \times 6} \]

\[ A = \frac{570}{42} \]

We can simplify this fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 570 and 42. The GCD of 570 and 42 is 6. So, we divide both the numerator and the denominator by 6:

\[ A = \frac{570 \div 6}{42 \div 6} \]

\[ A = \frac{95}{7} \]

Now, we need to find the area of the similar rectangle, which is \( \frac{18}{17} \) times bigger than the original rectangle. We multiply the area of the original rectangle by \( \frac{18}{17} \):

\[ \text{Area of similar rectangle} = \frac{95}{7} \times \frac{18}{17} \]

Again, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[ \text{Area of similar rectangle} = \frac{95 \times 18}{7 \times 17} \]

\[ \text{Area of similar rectangle} = \frac{1710}{119} \]

We can check if this fraction can be simplified. The GCD of 1710 and 119 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{1710}{119}\)

Expected answer: 1710/119

Correct? Yes

Problem: A soap factory produces 23/8 tonnes of soap each day. One day, they decided to increase production by an extra 4/20 of a tonne. However, later that same day, they reduce the production by 19/24 of a tonne due to a sudden power cut. How many tonnes of soap does the factory produce that day after these adjustments?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total production of soap after the adjustments, we need to follow these steps:

1. **Initial Production**: The factory produces \(\frac{23}{8}\) tonnes of soap each day.

2. **Increase in Production**: The factory increases production by \(\frac{4}{20}\) tonnes. Simplify \(\frac{4}{20}\):
   \[
   \frac{4}{20} = \frac{1}{5}
   \]

3. **Total Production after Increase**: Add the increased amount to the initial production:
   \[
   \frac{23}{8} + \frac{1}{5}
   \]

   To add these fractions, find a common denominator. The least common multiple of 8 and 5 is 40. Convert each fraction:
   \[
   \frac{23}{8} = \frac{23 \times 5}{8 \times 5} = \frac{115}{40}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{1}{5} = \frac{1 \times 8}{5 \times 8} = \frac{8}{40}
   \]

   Now add the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{115}{40} + \frac{8}{40} = \frac{123}{40}
   \]

4. **Reduction in Production**: The factory reduces production by \(\frac{19}{24}\) tonnes. Convert \(\frac{123}{40}\) and \(\frac{19}{24}\) to a common denominator. The least common multiple of 40 and 24 is 120. Convert each fraction:
   \[
   \frac{123}{40} = \frac{123 \times 3}{40 \times 3} = \frac{369}{120}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{19}{24} = \frac{19 \times 5}{24 \times 5} = \frac{95}{120}
   \]

   Now subtract the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{369}{120} - \frac{95}{120} = \frac{274}{120}
   \]

5. **Simplify the Result**: Simplify \(\frac{274}{120}\) by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 274 and 120, which is 2:
   \[
   \frac{274 \div 2}{120 \div 2} = \frac{137}{60}
   \]

Thus, the factory produces \(\frac{137}{60}\) tonnes of soap that day after the adjustments.

### Answer: \(\frac{137}{60}\) tonnes

Expected answer: 137/60

Correct? Yes

\[ \frac{24}{8} = 3 \text{ gallons} \]

So, the amount of red paint left in the machine, \( d \), is:
\[ d = 3 - 1.5 = 1.5 \text{ gallons} \]

The machine then adds \( \frac{1}{28} \) gallon of blue pigment. The total amount of paint, \( x \), is:
\[ x = d + \frac{1}{28} \]
\[ x = 1.5 + \frac{1}{28} \]

To add these, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 1.5 (which is \( \frac{3}{2} \)) and \( \frac{1}{28} \) is 28:
\[ 1.5 = \frac{3}{2} = \frac{3 \times 14}{2 \times 14} = \frac{42}{28} \]

Now, add the fractions:
\[ x = \frac{42}{28} + \frac{1}{28} = \frac{42 + 1}{28} = \frac{43}{28} \]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: A banana bread recipe requires you to multiply the fractions (27 / 14) and (17 / 13) together to determine how many ounces of mashed bananas you'll need. Compute the product of these fractions and write your answer as a simplified fraction to find out how many ounces are required.

GPT-4o: 

To find the product of the fractions \(\frac{27}{14}\) and \(\frac{17}{13}\), we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:

\[
\frac{27}{14} \times \frac{17}{13} = \frac{27 \times 17}{14 \times 13}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
27 \times 17 = 459
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
14 \times 13 = 182
\]

So, the product of the fractions is:

\[
\frac{459}{182}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 459 and 182. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 459 by 182 and find the remainder:
\[
459 \div 182 \approx 2.52 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
459 - 2 \times 182 = 459 - 364 = 95
\]

2. Now, divide 182 by 95 and find the remainder:
\[
182 \div 95 \approx 1.91 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
182 - 1 \times 95 = 182 - 95 = 87
\]

3. Next, divide 95 by 87 and find the remainder:
\[
95 \div 87 \approx 1.09 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
95 - 1 \times 87 = 95 - 87 = 8
\]

4. Finally, divide 87 by 8 and find the remainder:
\[
87 \div 8 \approx 10.875 \quad \text{(integer part is 10)}
\]
\[
87 - 10 \times 8 = 87 - 80 = 7
\]

5. Divide 8 by 7 and find the remainder:
\[
8 \div 7 \approx 1.14 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
8 - 1 \times 7 = 8 - 7 = 1
\]

Since the remainder is now 1, the GCD of 459 and 182 is 1. Therefore, the fraction \(\frac{459}{182}\) is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{459}{182}\)

Expected answer: 459/182

Correct? Yes

1. Divide 918 by 182 and find the remainder:
\[
918 \div 182 \approx 5.04 \quad \text{(integer part is 5)}
\]
\[
918 - 5 \times 182 = 918 - 910 = 8
\]

2. Now, divide 182 by 8 and find the remainder:
\[
182 \div 8 \approx 22.75 \quad \text{(integer part is 22)}
\]
\[
182 - 22 \times 8 = 182 - 176 = 6
\]

3. Next, divide 8 by 6 and find the remainder:
\[
8 \div 6 \approx 1.33 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
8 - 1 \times 6 = 8 - 6 = 2
\]

4. Finally, divide 6 by 2 and find the remainder:
\[
6 \div 2 = 3 \quad \text{(integer part is 3)}
\]
\[
6 - 3 \times 2 = 6 - 6 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 918 and 182 is 2. Therefore, we can simplify the fraction \(\frac{918}{182}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by 2:

\[
\frac{918 \div 2}{182 \div 2} = \frac{459}{91}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{459}{91}\)

Expected answer: 459/91

Correct? Yes

GPT-4o:

\[
\frac{27}{14} \times \frac{17}{15} = \frac{27 \times 17}{14 \times 15}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
27 \times 17 = 459
\]

Next, calculate the denominator:

\[
14 \times 15 = 210
\]

So, the product of the fractions is:

\[
\frac{459}{210}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 459 and 210. We can use the Euclidean algorithm to find the GCD.

1. Divide 459 by 210 and find the remainder:
\[
459 \div 210 \approx 2.19 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
459 - 2 \times 210 = 459 - 420 = 39
\]

2. Now, divide 210 by 39 and find the remainder:
\[
210 \div 39 \approx 5.38 \quad \text{(integer part is 5)}
\]
\[
210 - 5 \times 39 = 210 - 195 = 15
\]

3. Next, divide 39 by 15 and find the remainder:
\[
39 \div 15 \approx 2.6 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
39 - 2 \times 15 = 39 - 30 = 9
\]

4. Finally, divide 15 by 9 and find the remainder:
\[
15 \div 9 \approx 1.67 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
15 - 1 \times 9 = 15 - 9 = 6
\]

5. Divide 9 by 6 and find the remainder:
\[
9 \div 6 \approx 1.5 \quad \text{(integer part is 1)}
\]
\[
9 - 1 \times 6 = 9 - 6 = 3
\]

6. Divide 6 by 3 and find the remainder:
\[
6 \div 3 = 2 \quad \text{(integer part is 2)}
\]
\[
6 - 2 \times 3 = 6 - 6 = 0
\]

Since the remainder is now 0, the GCD of 459 and 210 is 3. Therefore, we can simplify the fraction \(\frac{459}{210}\) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their GCD, which is 3:

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Sonia uses 21/12 oz of toothpaste to brush her teeth every day. Her brother Anthony uses less toothpaste, just 6/27 oz daily. Add both quantities of toothpaste to get the total daily amount used by Sonia and Anthony. Now, suppose their mom includes an amount of toothpaste for herself to the total - she uses 3/18 oz of toothpaste daily. Add this amount to the total used by Sonia and Anthony to get the final total daily toothpaste usage for the whole family. Solve each fraction separately and give the answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's add the quantities of toothpaste used by Sonia and Anthony.

Sonia uses \( \frac{21}{12} \) oz of toothpaste daily.
Anthony uses \( \frac{6}{27} \) oz of toothpaste daily.

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 12 and 27 is 108.

Convert \( \frac{21}{12} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 108:
\[ \frac{21}{12} = \frac{21 \times 9}{12 \times 9} = \frac{189}{108} \]

Convert \( \frac{6}{27} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 108:
\[ \frac{6}{27} = \frac{6 \times 4}{27 \times 4} = \frac{24}{108} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{189}{108} + \frac{24}{108} = \frac{189 + 24}{108} = \frac{213}{108} \]

Next, simplify \( \frac{213}{108} \):
The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 213 and 108 is 3.
\[ \frac{213 \div 3}{108 \div 3} = \frac{71}{36} \]

Now, let's add the amount of toothpaste used by their mom, which is \( \frac{3}{18} \).

Convert \( \frac{3}{18} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 36:
\[ \frac{3}{18} = \frac{3 \times 2}{18 \times 2} = \frac{6}{36} \]

Now, add this to the previous total:
\[ \frac{71}{36} + \frac{6}{36} = \frac{71 + 6}{36} = \frac{77}{36} \]

Finally, simplify \( \frac{77}{36} \):
The GCD of 77 and 36 is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{77}{36}\)

Expected answer: 77/36

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Let's suppose for a special recipe sandwich, you need to divide a wheel of cheese into 14 equal parts and a pickle jar into 18 equal parts. To make one special sandwich, you need 21 parts of the wheel of cheese and 7 parts from the pickle jar. You've just made these sandwiches and you are down to ((7 / 18) + (21 / 14)) of your original ingredients. Later, you decided to make a simpler version of the sandwich which required half of the wheel of cheese and did not use any pickles. What fraction of the original ingredients do you have left after making the simpler sandwich? Calculate the answer by subtracting (2 / 4) from the fraction you had after making the first sandwich.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Calculate the fraction of the original ingredients left after making the special sandwiches.
2. Subtract the fraction used for the simpler sandwich from the remaining fraction.

First, let's calculate the fraction of the original ingredients left after making the special sandwiches:

Given:
- The fraction of the wheel of cheese left is \(\frac{21}{14}\).
- The fraction of the pickle jar left is \(\frac{7}{18}\).

We need to add these fractions together:
\[
\frac{21}{14} + \frac{7}{18}
\]

First, simplify \(\frac{21}{14}\):
\[
\frac{21}{14} = \frac{21 \div 7}{14 \div 7} = \frac{3}{2}
\]

Now, add \(\frac{3}{2}\) and \(\frac{7}{18}\). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 2 and 18 is 18.

Convert \(\frac{3}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 18:
\[
\frac{3}{2} = \frac{3 \times 9}{2 \times 9} = \frac{27}{18}
\]

Now add the fractions:
\[
\frac{27}{18} + \frac{7}{18} = \frac{27 + 7}{18} = \frac{34}{18}
\]

Simplify \(\frac{34}{18}\):
\[
\frac{34}{18} = \frac{34 \div 2}{18 \div 2} = \frac{17}{9}
\]

Next, we need to subtract the fraction used for the simpler sandwich. The simpler sandwich uses half of the wheel of cheese, which is \(\frac{1}{2}\) or \(\frac{2}{4}\).

Convert \(\frac{2}{4}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 9:
\[
\frac{2}{4} = \frac{2 \times 9}{4 \times 9} = \frac{18}{36} = \frac{1}{2}
\]

Now, subtract \(\frac{1}{2}\) from \(\frac{17}{9}\). Convert \(\frac{1}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 9:
\[
\frac{1}{2} = \frac{1 \times 9}{2 \times 9} = \frac{9}{18}
\]

Subtract:
\[
\frac{17}{9} - \frac{9}{18}
\]

Convert \(\frac{9}{18}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 9:
\[
\frac{9}{18} = \frac{9 \div 9}{18 \div 9} = \frac{1}{2} = \frac{9}{18}
\]

Now, subtract:
\[
\frac{17}{9} - \frac{9}{18} = \frac{34}{18} - \frac{9}{18} = \frac{34 - 9}{18} = \frac{25}{18}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{25}{18}\)

Expected answer: 25/18

Correct? Yes

\[ 2.25 \text{ hours} + 13 \text{ hours} + 3.75 \text{ hours} \]

\[ 2.25 + 13 + 3.75 = 19 \text{ hours} \]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Jeremy went to a sandwich shop that slices cheese by weight measured in ounces. He ordered slices of cheese that weighed 30/9 ounces in total. However, upon weighing, he found that there was 17/22 ounces less cheese than he requested. Calculate how much cheese he actually received. Use the equation 'd = n - (17 / 22)' to find the answer.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much cheese Jeremy actually received, we start with the total weight of cheese he ordered, which is \( \frac{30}{9} \) ounces. We need to subtract the amount of cheese that was missing, which is \( \frac{17}{22} \) ounces.

First, simplify \( \frac{30}{9} \):
\[ \frac{30}{9} = \frac{10}{3} \]

Next, we need to subtract \( \frac{17}{22} \) from \( \frac{10}{3} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 3 and 22 is 66.

Convert \( \frac{10}{3} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 66:
\[ \frac{10}{3} = \frac{10 \times 22}{3 \times 22} = \frac{220}{66} \]

Convert \( \frac{17}{22} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 66:
\[ \frac{17}{22} = \frac{17 \times 3}{22 \times 3} = \frac{51}{66} \]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[ \frac{220}{66} - \frac{51}{66} = \frac{220 - 51}{66} = \frac{169}{66} \]

Thus, Jeremy actually received \( \frac{169}{66} \) ounces of cheese.

### Answer: \(\frac{169}{66}\) ounces

Expected answer: 169/66

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Following the previous problem, Jeremy decided to make sandwiches for his friends. Each of his friends wanted a sandwich that had (30 / 18) ounces of the cheese Jeremy received from the shop. Calculate the total amount of cheese in ounces that Jeremy will have to use if he uses 'd' ounces of cheese from what he received for each sandwich. Use the formula 'k = (30 / 18) * d' to find your answer.

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total amount of cheese Jeremy will use for each sandwich, we start with the formula \( k = \frac{30}{18} \times d \), where \( d \) is the amount of cheese Jeremy received, which we previously calculated as \( \frac{169}{66} \) ounces.

First, simplify \( \frac{30}{18} \):
\[ \frac{30}{18} = \frac{5}{3} \]

Now, substitute \( d = \frac{169}{66} \) into the formula:
\[ k = \frac{5}{3} \times \frac{169}{66} \]

To multiply these fractions, multiply the numerators and the denominators:
\[ k = \frac{5 \times 169}{3 \times 66} = \frac{845}{198} \]

Thus, the total amount of cheese Jeremy will use for each sandwich is \( \frac{845}{198} \) ounces.

With this change, calculate how much cheese he actually received now. Use the equation 'd = n - (20 / 22)' to find the answer.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much cheese Jeremy actually received with the new discrepancy, we start with the total weight of cheese he ordered, which is \( \frac{30}{9} \) ounces. We need to subtract the new amount of cheese that was missing, which is \( \frac{20}{22} \) ounces.

First, simplify \( \frac{30}{9} \):
\[ \frac{30}{9} = \frac{10}{3} \]

Convert \( \frac{20}{22} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 66:
\[ \frac{20}{22} = \frac{20 \times 3}{22 \times 3} = \frac{60}{66} \]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[ \frac{220}{66} - \frac{60}{66} = \frac{220 - 60}{66} = \frac{160}{66} \]

Simplify the fraction \( \frac{160}{66} \):
\[ \frac{160}{66} = \frac{80}{33} \]

Thus, Jeremy actually received \( \frac{80}{33} \) ounces of cheese.

### Answer: \(\frac{80}{33}\) ounces

Expected answer: 80/33

Correct? Yes

Problem: Sophia is a researcher who studies sunglasses. She was examining a batch of sunglasses and trying to calculate the average light blocking efficiency. In the first test, she found that 13 out of every 4 sunglasses blocked all UV rays completely, while in the second test, 20 out of every 18 sunglasses also blocked all UV rays. Sophia decided to add these numbers to her total. Next, she added the additional 21 out of 17 sunglasses from another batch that also blocked all UV rays. Later, she realized she made a mistake and needed to subtract the 16 out of 30 sunglasses that actually did not block all UV rays. What is the final corrected number of sunglasses that blocked all UV rays, according to Sophia's tests and calculations? Please give your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to add and subtract the fractions representing the sunglasses that blocked all UV rays and those that did not.

First, let's convert all the given fractions to a common denominator to make the calculations easier.

1. The first test result is \( \frac{13}{4} \).
2. The second test result is \( \frac{20}{18} \), which simplifies to \( \frac{10}{9} \).
3. The additional batch result is \( \frac{21}{17} \).
4. The incorrect batch result is \( \frac{16}{30} \), which simplifies to \( \frac{8}{15} \).

Now, we need to find a common denominator for these fractions. The least common multiple (LCM) of 4, 9, 17, and 15 is 3060.

Let's convert each fraction to have the denominator 3060:

1. \( \frac{13}{4} = \frac{13 \times 765}{4 \times 765} = \frac{9945}{3060} \)
2. \( \frac{10}{9} = \frac{10 \times 340}{9 \times 340} = \frac{3400}{3060} \)
3. \( \frac{21}{17} = \frac{21 \times 180}{17 \times 180} = \frac{3780}{3060} \)
4. \( \frac{8}{15} = \frac{8 \times 204}{15 \times 204} = \frac{1632}{3060} \)

Now, we add the fractions that represent sunglasses blocking all UV rays and subtract the fraction that represents sunglasses not blocking all UV rays:

\[
\frac{9945}{3060} + \frac{3400}{3060} + \frac{3780}{3060} - \frac{1632}{3060}
\]

Combine the numerators:

\[
9945 + 3400 + 3780 - 1632 = 15493
\]

So, the combined fraction is:

\[
\frac{15493}{3060}

This fraction is already in its simplest form because 15493 and 3060 have no common factors other than 1.

\]

8. \(3 \div 2 \approx 1\) with a remainder of \(3 - 2 = 1\)

Problem: Shawn is making sandwiches for a picnic. The recipe for the sandwiches requires different amounts of mayonnaise and sandwich spread. To make a sandwich, Shawn uses 23/28 cups of mayonnaise and 6/9 cups of sandwich spread. How many cups of these two ingredients does Shawn use in total to make a sandwich? While preparing the sandwiches, Shawn realizes that he has to add 18/12 cups of cheese spread to his recipe. Calculate the total amount of ingredients Shawn now needs to make one sandwich which includes mayonnaise, sandwich spread, and cheese spread. Finally, if Shawn has to make an equal number of sandwiches using 4/4 cups of all the ingredients combined, how many cups of ingredients will he use in total to make those sandwiches?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's find the total amount of mayonnaise and sandwich spread Shawn uses for one sandwich.

1. **Mayonnaise:**
   \[
   \frac{23}{28} \text{ cups}
   \]

2. **Sandwich spread:**
   \[
   \frac{6}{9} = \frac{2}{3} \text{ cups}
   \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 28 and 3 is 84.

Convert \(\frac{23}{28}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 84:
\[
\frac{23}{28} = \frac{23 \times 3}{28 \times 3} = \frac{69}{84}
\]

Convert \(\frac{2}{3}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 84:
\[
\frac{2}{3} = \frac{2 \times 28}{3 \times 28} = \frac{56}{84}
\]

Now, add the fractions:
\[
\frac{69}{84} + \frac{56}{84} = \frac{69 + 56}{84} = \frac{125}{84}
\]

So, the total amount of mayonnaise and sandwich spread is:
\[
\frac{125}{84} \text{ cups}
\]

Next, we add the cheese spread:
\[
\frac{18}{12} = \frac{3 \times 6}{2 \times 6} = \frac{3}{2} = \frac{126}{84}
\]

Now, add this to the previous total:
\[
\frac{125}{84} + \frac{126}{84} = \frac{125 + 126}{84} = \frac{251}{84}
\]

So, the total amount of ingredients for one sandwich is:
\[
\frac{251}{84} \text{ cups}
\]

Finally, if Shawn uses 4/4 cups of all ingredients combined to make an equal number of sandwiches, we need to determine how many sandwiches he can make with \(\frac{4}{4} = 1\) cup of ingredients.

To find the number of sandwiches:
\[
\frac{1}{\frac{251}{84}} = \frac{84}{251}
\]

Thus, the total amount of ingredients used to make these sandwiches is:
\[
\frac{84}{251} \times 1 = \frac{84}{251} \text{ cups}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{84}{251}\) cups

Expected answer: 251/84

Correct? No

Problem: Cassandra collected keys for a hobby. At first she had a collection equivalent to 7/6 of a key set. After she lost 1/21 of a key set, how many key sets does she have now?

GPT-4o: 

To determine how many key sets Cassandra has now, we need to follow these steps:

1. Start with the initial number of key sets Cassandra had, which is \( \frac{7}{6} \) of a key set.
2. Subtract the number of key sets she lost, which is \( \frac{1}{21} \) of a key set.

First, we need a common denominator to subtract these fractions. The least common multiple of 6 and 21 is 42.

Convert \( \frac{7}{6} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 42:
\[ \frac{7}{6} = \frac{7 \times 7}{6 \times 7} = \frac{49}{42} \]

Convert \( \frac{1}{21} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 42:
\[ \frac{1}{21} = \frac{1 \times 2}{21 \times 2} = \frac{2}{42} \]

Now, subtract \( \frac{2}{42} \) from \( \frac{49}{42} \):
\[ \frac{49}{42} - \frac{2}{42} = \frac{49 - 2}{42} = \frac{47}{42} \]

So, Cassandra now has \( \frac{47}{42} \) of a key set.

### Answer: \(\frac{47}{42}\)

Expected answer: 47/42

Correct? Yes

Problem: A songwriter is composing a new piece. In the first section, he uses a ratio of 29 notes every 23 measures. In the second section, he uses a ratio of 19 notes every 17 measures. Calculate the difference between the sum of the ratios of the two sections ((29 / 23) + (19 / 17)) and the ratio of a rest, which is equivalent to one whole measure (26/26), used in the third section of his composition.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to calculate the sum of the ratios of the two sections and then find the difference between this sum and the ratio of a rest used in the third section.

First, let's calculate the sum of the ratios of the two sections:

1. The ratio of notes to measures in the first section is \( \frac{29}{23} \).
2. The ratio of notes to measures in the second section is \( \frac{19}{17} \).

We add these two ratios together:

\[
\frac{29}{23} + \frac{19}{17}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 23 and 17 is 391 (since 23 and 17 are both prime numbers, their LCM is their product).

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 391:

\[
\frac{29}{23} = \frac{29 \times 17}{23 \times 17} = \frac{493}{391}
\]

\[
\frac{19}{17} = \frac{19 \times 23}{17 \times 23} = \frac{437}{391}
\]

Now, add the fractions:

\[
\frac{493}{391} + \frac{437}{391} = \frac{493 + 437}{391} = \frac{930}{391}
\]

Next, we need to find the difference between this sum and the ratio of a rest, which is \( \frac{26}{26} \) (equivalent to 1):

\[
\frac{930}{391} - \frac{26}{26}
\]

Since \( \frac{26}{26} = 1 \), we can rewrite the expression as:

\[
\frac{930}{391} - 1
\]

Convert 1 to a fraction with the same denominator:

\[
1 = \frac{391}{391}
\]

Now, subtract the fractions:

\[
\frac{930}{391} - \frac{391}{391} = \frac{930 - 391}{391} = \frac{539}{391}
\]

Thus, the difference between the sum of the ratios of the two sections and the ratio of a rest used in the third section is:

### Answer: \(\frac{539}{391}\)

Expected answer: 539/391

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: A car travels 21/4 miles every hour. One day, the car was needed to travel an extra 16/13 miles, but due to a detour, it only traveled an additional 1/21 miles. How many more miles was the car supposed to travel in total that day, given that it ran continuously at the same speed? Calculate by multiplying the additional distance needed by the average miles the car travels in an hour.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine the additional distance the car was supposed to travel. The car was supposed to travel an extra \( \frac{16}{13} \) miles, but it only traveled an additional \( \frac{1}{21} \) miles. 

To find the difference, we need to subtract \( \frac{1}{21} \) from \( \frac{16}{13} \):

\[
\frac{16}{13} - \frac{1}{21}
\]

To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 13 and 21 is 273. We convert each fraction:

\[
\frac{16}{13} = \frac{16 \times 21}{13 \times 21} = \frac{336}{273}
\]

\[
\frac{1}{21} = \frac{1 \times 13}{21 \times 13} = \frac{13}{273}
\]

Now, subtract the fractions:

\[
\frac{336}{273} - \frac{13}{273} = \frac{336 - 13}{273} = \frac{323}{273}
\]

Next, we need to calculate how many more miles the car was supposed to travel in total that day. The car travels \( \frac{21}{4} \) miles every hour. We multiply this speed by the additional distance:

\[
\frac{21}{4} \times \frac{323}{273}
\]

First, simplify the multiplication:

\[
\frac{21 \times 323}{4 \times 273}
\]

Calculate the numerator and the denominator:

\[
21 \times 323 = 6783
\]

\[
4 \times 273 = 1092
\]

So, the fraction becomes:

\[
\frac{6783}{1092}
\]

Simplify the fraction by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 6783 and 1092. The GCD is 21:

\[
\frac{6783 \div 21}{1092 \div 21} = \frac{323}{52}
\]

Thus, the car was supposed to travel an additional \( \frac{323}{52} \) miles.

### Answer: \(\frac{323}{52}\) miles.

Expected answer: 323/52

Correct? Yes

\frac{16}{6} - \frac{1}{21}
\]

First, simplify \( \frac{16}{6} \):

\[
\frac{16}{6} = \frac{8}{3}
\]

Now, we need a common denominator to subtract these fractions. The least common multiple of 3 and 21 is 21. We convert each fraction:

\[
\frac{8}{3} = \frac{8 \times 7}{3 \times 7} = \frac{56}{21}
\]

\[
\frac{1}{21} = \frac{1}{21}
\]

Now, subtract the fractions:

\[
\frac{56}{21} - \frac{1}{21} = \frac{56 - 1}{21} = \frac{55}{21}
\]

Next, we need to calculate how many more miles the car was supposed to travel in total that day. The car travels \( \frac{21}{4} \) miles every hour. We multiply this speed by the additional distance:

\[
\frac{21}{4} \times \frac{55}{21}
\]

First, simplify the multiplication:

\[
\frac{21 \times 55}{4 \times 21}
\]

The 21s cancel out:

\[
\frac{55}{4}
\]

Thus, the car was supposed to travel an additional \( \frac{55}{4} \) miles.

### Answer: \(\frac{55}{4}\) miles.

Expected answer: 55/4

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: In a book publishing company, the manager has to look after various departments. The editing team takes 20/5 hours to edit a manuscript of a book, while the typesetting team needs 18/17 hours to adjust the layout of a page. Some break delay happens that results in a collective loss of 6/15 hours. After these delays and losses, the manager, to compensate, extended the working hours by the same amount of time as the initial time span of the process. On a particular day, they continue to work. What's the total extended time in hours, if you multiply the time required for the entire process and the extended time after the reduction of the lost hours with the initial total time required?

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Calculate the time taken by the editing team to edit a manuscript.
2. Calculate the time taken by the typesetting team to adjust the layout of a page.
3. Sum these times to get the initial total time required for the process.
4. Subtract the collective loss due to breaks.
5. Determine the extended time, which is equal to the initial total time required.
6. Multiply the initial total time required by the extended time after the reduction of the lost hours.

Let's go through each step in detail:

1. **Time taken by the editing team:**
   \[
   \text{Time taken by the editing team} = \frac{20}{5} \text{ hours} = 4 \text{ hours}
   \]

2. **Time taken by the typesetting team:**
   \[
   \text{Time taken by the typesetting team} = \frac{18}{17} \text{ hours}
   \]

3. **Initial total time required:**
   \[
   \text{Initial total time required} = 4 \text{ hours} + \frac{18}{17} \text{ hours}
   \]
   To add these times, we need a common denominator:
   \[
   4 = \frac{68}{17}
   \]
   So,
   \[
   \text{Initial total time required} = \frac{68}{17} + \frac{18}{17} = \frac{86}{17} \text{ hours}
   \]

4. **Subtract the collective loss due to breaks:**
   \[
   \text{Collective loss} = \frac{6}{15} \text{ hours} = \frac{2}{5} \text{ hours}
   \]
   Subtracting this from the initial total time:
   \[
   \text{Adjusted time} = \frac{86}{17} - \frac{2}{5}
   \]
   To subtract these, we need a common denominator:
   \[
   \frac{86}{17} = \frac{86 \times 5}{17 \times 5} = \frac{430}{85}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{2}{5} = \frac{2 \times 17}{5 \times 17} = \frac{34}{85}
   \]
   So,
   \[
   \text{Adjusted time} = \frac{430}{85} - \frac{34}{85} = \frac{396}{85} \text{ hours}
   \]

5. **Extended time (equal to the initial total time required):**
   \[
   \text{Extended time} = \frac{86}{17} \text{ hours}
   \]

6. **Multiply the initial total time required by the extended time after the reduction of the lost hours:**
   \[
   \text{Total extended time} = \left(\frac{86}{17}\right) \times \left(\frac{396}{85}\right)
   \]
   Simplify the multiplication:
   \[
   \frac{86}{17} = 5.058823529
   \]
   \[
   \frac{396}{85} = 4.658823529
   \]
   \[
   5.058823529 \times 4.658823529 = 23.56
   \]

### Answer: 23.56

Expected answer: 34056/1445

Correct? No

Problem: Jenny plants 13/11 rows of potatoes in her garden. Each row yields approximately 21/3 bushels. If Jenny sells her yield at the farmer's market where each bushel earns her 21/15 dollars, how many dollars will she make in total by selling all her potatoes?

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much Jenny will make in total by selling all her potatoes, we need to follow these steps:

1. Calculate the total number of bushels Jenny yields.
2. Calculate the total earnings from selling the bushels.

\frac{21}{15} = \frac{7}{5}

\]

So, the sum of the amount of gold and silver used by the jeweler is 1 kilogram.

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: In a beehive, there are sections for honey storage and bee rearing. Each section is classified into many sub-sections. One day, the beekeeper discovered that each honey storage sub-section had (25 / 9) gallons of honey. He also found the same amount of honey in each bee rearing sub-section. If he combined the honey from both a honey storage sub-section and a bee rearing sub-section, the beekeeper would have a total quantity represented by 'p'. However, one honey storage sub-section had an additional (2 / 26) gallons of honey. So, if the beekeeper was calculating the total amount from this sub-section plus a bee rearing sub-section, the total amount of honey would be defined as 's'. What quantity of honey ('s') would the beekeeper have in total from this scenario?

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to determine the total amount of honey in the combined sub-sections under the given conditions.

First, let's denote the amount of honey in each honey storage sub-section and each bee rearing sub-section as \( h \).

Given:
\[ h = \frac{25}{9} \text{ gallons} \]

When the beekeeper combines the honey from one honey storage sub-section and one bee rearing sub-section, the total amount of honey \( p \) is:
\[ p = h + h = \frac{25}{9} + \frac{25}{9} = \frac{50}{9} \text{ gallons} \]

Now, consider the scenario where one honey storage sub-section has an additional \( \frac{2}{26} \) gallons of honey. The total amount of honey in this honey storage sub-section is:
\[ h + \frac{2}{26} = \frac{25}{9} + \frac{2}{26} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 9 and 26 is 234. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{25}{9} = \frac{25 \times 26}{9 \times 26} = \frac{650}{234} \]
\[ \frac{2}{26} = \frac{2 \times 9}{26 \times 9} = \frac{18}{234} \]

Now, add these fractions:
\[ \frac{650}{234} + \frac{18}{234} = \frac{650 + 18}{234} = \frac{668}{234} \]

Simplify the fraction:
\[ \frac{668}{234} = \frac{334}{117} \]

Thus, the total amount of honey \( s \) in this scenario, combining the honey from this honey storage sub-section and a bee rearing sub-section, is:
\[ s = \frac{334}{117} + \frac{25}{9} \]

Convert \( \frac{25}{9} \) to have the same denominator:
\[ \frac{25}{9} = \frac{25 \times 13}{9 \times 13} = \frac{325}{117} \]

Add the fractions:
\[ s = \frac{334}{117} + \frac{325}{117} = \frac{334 + 325}{117} = \frac{659}{117} \]

Simplify the fraction:
\[ \frac{659}{117} = \frac{659 \div 1}{117 \div 1} = \frac{659}{117} \]

Thus, the quantity of honey \( s \) the beekeeper would have in total from this scenario is:
\[ s = \frac{659}{117} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{659}{117}\) gallons

Expected answer: 659/117

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Instead of each sub-section having (25 / 9) gallons of honey, they each actually had (25 / 4) gallons of honey. This new quantity is represented by 'r'. When he combines the honey from a honey storage sub-section and a bee rearing sub-section, the total amount of honey is now represented by 'p'. However, the particular honey storage sub-section that had an additional (2 / 26) gallons of honey has changed. This new quantity is represented by 's'. \[ r = \frac{25}{4} \text{ gallons} \]

When the beekeeper combines the honey from one honey storage sub-section and one bee rearing sub-section, the total amount of honey \( p \) is:
\[ p = r + r = \frac{25}{4} + \frac{25}{4} = \frac{50}{4} = 12.5 \text{ gallons} \]

Now, consider the scenario where one honey storage sub-section has an additional \( \frac{2}{26} \) gallons of honey. The total amount of honey in this honey storage sub-section is:
\[ r + \frac{2}{26} = \frac{25}{4} + \frac{2}{26} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 4 and 26 is 52. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[ \frac{25}{4} = \frac{25 \times 13}{4 \times 13} = \frac{325}{52} \]
\[ \frac{2}{26} = \frac{2 \times 2}{26 \times 2} = \frac{4}{52} \]

Thus, the total amount of honey \( s \) in this scenario, combining the honey from this honey storage sub-section and a bee rearing sub-section, is:
\[ s = \frac{329}{52} + \frac{25}{4} \]

\[ s = \frac{329}{52} + \frac{325}{52} = \frac{329 + 325}{52} = \frac{654}{52} \]

Simplify the fraction:
\[ \frac{654}{52} = \frac{654 \div 2}{52 \div 2} = \frac{327}{26} \]

Thus, the quantity of honey \( s \) the beekeeper would have in total from this scenario is:
\[ s = \frac{327}{26} \]

GPT-4o: 

To find the total pounds of fish the bear ate over the three days, we need to add the fractions:

1. First day: \( \frac{28}{6} \)
2. Second day: \( \frac{21}{18} \)
3. Third day: \( \frac{24}{22} \)

   \[
   \frac{28}{6} = \frac{14}{3}
   \]

   \[
   \frac{21}{18} = \frac{7}{6}
   \]

   \[
   \frac{24}{22} = \frac{12}{11}
   \]

1. \( \frac{14}{3} \):
   \[
   \frac{14}{3} = \frac{14 \times 22}{3 \times 22} = \frac{308}{66}
   \]

Problem: Heather was preparing a special three-course dinner for her family. For the first course, she had a bread recipe that required 11/17 of a cup of sugar. In addition, she baked a custard for dessert that required another 6/2 cups of sugar. As her family loves sweet dishes, she decided to increase the total quantity of sugar by a factor of 29/21. How many cups of sugar did Heather use in total?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine the total amount of sugar Heather used in her recipes before increasing the quantity.

For the bread recipe, she used:
\[ \frac{11}{17} \text{ cups of sugar} \]

For the custard, she used:
\[ \frac{6}{2} = 3 \text{ cups of sugar} \]

Adding these amounts together:
\[ \frac{11}{17} + 3 \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 17 and 1 (since 3 can be written as \(\frac{3}{1}\)) is 17.

Convert 3 to a fraction with a denominator of 17:
\[ 3 = \frac{3 \times 17}{1 \times 17} = \frac{51}{17} \]

Now add the fractions:
\[ \frac{11}{17} + \frac{51}{17} = \frac{11 + 51}{17} = \frac{62}{17} \]

Next, Heather decided to increase the total quantity of sugar by a factor of \(\frac{29}{21}\). So, we multiply the total amount of sugar by this factor:
\[ \frac{62}{17} \times \frac{29}{21} \]

Multiply the numerators and the denominators:
\[ \frac{62 \times 29}{17 \times 21} = \frac{1798}{357} \]

To simplify \(\frac{1798}{357}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1798 and 357. The GCD is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

Thus, the total amount of sugar Heather used is:
\[ \frac{1798}{357} \approx 5.04 \text{ cups} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{1798}{357}\) cups

Problem: King Arthur is planning a grand feast at his castle. He estimates that each guest will consume 15/7 gallons of water and 15/24 gallons of wine. On the other hand, the royal baker needs 26/20 gallons of milk for each of the cakes he's baking. Calculate the total amount of liquid (v) that will be consumed if the baker's requirement is multiplied by the guests' consumption (i), and then add this to the guests' consumption (v) to find the total amount of liquid (x) needed for the feast.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow these steps:

1. Calculate the total amount of liquid each guest will consume.
2. Calculate the total amount of liquid the baker needs for each cake.
3. Multiply the baker's requirement by the guests' consumption.
4. Add the result to the guests' consumption to find the total amount of liquid needed.

Let's start with the guests' consumption:

1. Each guest consumes \( \frac{15}{7} \) gallons of water and \( \frac{15}{24} \) gallons of wine.
   - Total liquid per guest: 
   \[
   \frac{15}{7} + \frac{15}{24}
   \]

   To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 7 and 24 is 168.

   - Convert \( \frac{15}{7} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 168:
   \[
   \frac{15}{7} = \frac{15 \times 24}{7 \times 24} = \frac{360}{168}
   \]

   - Convert \( \frac{15}{24} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 168:
   \[
   \frac{15}{24} = \frac{15 \times 7}{24 \times 7} = \frac{105}{168}
   \]

   - Add the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{360}{168} + \frac{105}{168} = \frac{360 + 105}{168} = \frac{465}{168}
   \]

2. The baker needs \( \frac{26}{20} \) gallons of milk for each cake.
   - Simplify \( \frac{26}{20} \):
   \[
   \frac{26}{20} = \frac{13}{10}
   \]

3. Multiply the baker's requirement by the guests' consumption:
   - Multiply \( \frac{13}{10} \) by \( \frac{465}{168} \):
   \[
   \frac{13}{10} \times \frac{465}{168} = \frac{13 \times 465}{10 \times 168} = \frac{6045}{1680}
   \]

4. Add the result to the guests' consumption:
   - Convert \( \frac{465}{168} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 1680:
   \[
   \frac{465}{168} = \frac{465 \times 10}{168 \times 10} = \frac{4650}{1680}
   \]

   - Add the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{4650}{1680} + \frac{6045}{1680} = \frac{4650 + 6045}{1680} = \frac{10695}{1680}
   \]

   - Simplify \( \frac{10695}{1680} \):
   \[
   \frac{10695}{1680} = \frac{10695 \div 15}{1680 \div 15} = \frac{713}{112}
   \]

### Answer: \(\frac{713}{112}\)

Expected answer: 713/112

Correct? Yes
