Problem: Teddy is a bear who loves to play with numbers. One day, Teddy was playing with his favorite number, which just so happened to be 30/17. While playing, he saw another number, 18/15, and decided to add it to his favorite number. With this new number in mind, he then saw another, 24/13, and decided to multiply it by his new number. What is Teddy's final number?

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to follow the steps of addition and multiplication with fractions.

First, let's add the two fractions \( \frac{30}{17} \) and \( \frac{18}{15} \).

1. Find a common denominator for the fractions \( \frac{30}{17} \) and \( \frac{18}{15} \). The least common multiple (LCM) of 17 and 15 is 255.

2. Convert each fraction to have the common denominator:
   \[
   \frac{30}{17} = \frac{30 \times 15}{17 \times 15} = \frac{450}{255}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{18}{15} = \frac{18 \times 17}{15 \times 17} = \frac{306}{255}
   \]

3. Add the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{450}{255} + \frac{306}{255} = \frac{450 + 306}{255} = \frac{756}{255}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction \( \frac{756}{255} \):
   \[
   \frac{756 \div 3}{255 \div 3} = \frac{252}{85}
   \]

Next, we need to multiply this result by \( \frac{24}{13} \).

5. Multiply the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{252}{85} \times \frac{24}{13} = \frac{252 \times 24}{85 \times 13} = \frac{6048}{1105}
   \]

Thus, Teddy's final number is \( \frac{6048}{1105} \).

### Answer: \(\frac{6048}{1105}\)

Expected answer: 6048/1105

Correct? Yes

The desired diameter is given as:
\[ \frac{20}{6} \text{ cm} \]

The diameter of the drill bit is:
\[ \frac{11}{21} \text{ cm} \]

To find the fraction of the desired diameter that each hole would have, we divide the diameter of the drill bit by the desired diameter:
\[ \frac{\frac{11}{21}}{\frac{20}{6}} \]

To divide by a fraction, we multiply by its reciprocal:
\[ \frac{11}{21} \times \frac{6}{20} \]

Now, we multiply the numerators and the denominators:
\[ \frac{11 \times 6}{21 \times 20} = \frac{66}{420} \]

Thus, each hole drilled with the current drill bit would be:
\[ \frac{66}{420} \]

Problem: Aaron has a small model car collection. His favorite car model takes exactly 17/10 hours to assemble. He started assembling a new car model and realized that it was simpler, taking only 12/23 hours to complete. How much less time, in hours, will the second model take than the first one? Write your answer as a simplified fraction or decimal.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much less time the second model takes compared to the first one, we need to subtract the time taken for the second model from the time taken for the first model.

First, let's convert the fractions to a common denominator to make the subtraction easier. The denominators are 10 and 23. The least common multiple (LCM) of 10 and 23 is 230.

Convert \( \frac{17}{10} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 230:
\[ \frac{17}{10} = \frac{17 \times 23}{10 \times 23} = \frac{391}{230} \]

Convert \( \frac{12}{23} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 230:
\[ \frac{12}{23} = \frac{12 \times 10}{23 \times 10} = \frac{120}{230} \]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[ \frac{391}{230} - \frac{120}{230} = \frac{391 - 120}{230} = \frac{271}{230} \]

The fraction \( \frac{271}{230} \) is already in its simplest form because 271 is a prime number and does not share any common factors with 230.

Thus, the second model takes \( \frac{271}{230} \) hours less than the first model.

### Answer: \( \frac{271}{230} \)

Expected answer: 271/230

Correct? Yes

Problem: Carlos is very handy, and he decided to start a business making and selling chairs. He usually makes each chair using 20/15 units of wood. For a special order, he decided to design a larger, sturdier chair that uses (24/5) times (7/6) units more wood than usual. In total, how many units of wood would Carlos need to make one of these special chairs? Please give your answer in simplest form.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine how much additional wood Carlos needs for the special chair. The additional wood required is given by the product of \(\frac{24}{5}\) and \(\frac{7}{6}\).

\[
\frac{24}{5} \times \frac{7}{6} = \frac{24 \times 7}{5 \times 6} = \frac{168}{30}
\]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{168}{30}\) by finding the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 168 and 30. The GCD of 168 and 30 is 6.

\[
\frac{168 \div 6}{30 \div 6} = \frac{28}{5}
\]

So, the additional wood required is \(\frac{28}{5}\) units.

Now, we need to add this to the usual amount of wood Carlos uses for a chair, which is \(\frac{20}{15}\). We simplify \(\frac{20}{15}\) first:

\[
\frac{20}{15} = \frac{4}{3}
\]

Now, we add \(\frac{4}{3}\) and \(\frac{28}{5}\). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 3 and 5 is 15.

\[
\frac{4}{3} = \frac{4 \times 5}{3 \times 5} = \frac{20}{15}
\]

\[
\frac{28}{5} = \frac{28 \times 3}{5 \times 3} = \frac{84}{15}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:

\[
\frac{20}{15} + \frac{84}{15} = \frac{20 + 84}{15} = \frac{104}{15}
\]

Thus, Carlos needs \(\frac{104}{15}\) units of wood to make one of these special chairs.

### Answer: \(\frac{104}{15}\)

Expected answer: 104/15

Problem: Officer Davis was monitoring traffic for speeders. He was measuring the speed of cars passing by him using a radar gun. The gun showed one car was going 13/4 miles per minute. Suddenly, the car slows down and reduces his speed by 14/15 miles per minute. Officer Davis noted down the new speed of the car. Suddenly, the car increased its speed again by 30/15 miles per minute. What was the final speed of the car according to Officer Davis's radar gun?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the final speed of the car, we need to follow these steps:

1. **Initial Speed**: The car was initially going at \( \frac{13}{4} \) miles per minute.

2. **Speed Reduction**: The car then reduced its speed by \( \frac{14}{15} \) miles per minute. We need to subtract this from the initial speed:
   \[
   \frac{13}{4} - \frac{14}{15}
   \]

   To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 4 and 15 is 60. We convert both fractions to have this common denominator:
   \[
   \frac{13}{4} = \frac{13 \times 15}{4 \times 15} = \frac{195}{60}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{14}{15} = \frac{14 \times 4}{15 \times 4} = \frac{56}{60}
   \]

   Now, subtract the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{195}{60} - \frac{56}{60} = \frac{195 - 56}{60} = \frac{139}{60}
   \]

3. **Speed Increase**: The car then increased its speed by \( \frac{30}{15} \) miles per minute. Simplify \( \frac{30}{15} \):
   \[
   \frac{30}{15} = 2
   \]

   We need to add this to the current speed:
   \[
   \frac{139}{60} + 2
   \]

   Convert 2 to a fraction with a denominator of 60:
   \[
   2 = \frac{120}{60}
   \]

   Now, add the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{139}{60} + \frac{120}{60} = \frac{139 + 120}{60} = \frac{259}{60}
   \]

Thus, the final speed of the car according to Officer Davis's radar gun is \( \frac{259}{60} \) miles per minute.

### Answer: \(\frac{259}{60}\) miles per minute

Expected answer: 259/60

Correct? Yes

Problem: Jake is trying to figure out how many grapes he can get from a certain vineyard. - The vineyard can usually produce 19/2 baskets of grapes every season. However, due to weather conditions, only 19/29 of the usual amount were produced this season. How many baskets of grapes were produced this season? - But Jake isn't the only one interested in these grapes. He has to share the grapes with others. He gets to keep only 7/11 of the total amount of grapes. How many baskets of grapes does he get? - Out of the grapes that he got, Jake wants to make some grape juice. But he only uses 9/10 of his grapes to make the juice. How many baskets of grapes does he use for the juice?

GPT-4o: 

Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. **Calculating the number of baskets produced this season:**
   - The usual production is \( \frac{19}{2} \) baskets.
   - This season, only \( \frac{19}{29} \) of the usual amount was produced.
   - To find the number of baskets produced this season, we multiply the usual production by the fraction produced this season:
     \[
     \text{Baskets produced this season} = \left( \frac{19}{2} \right) \times \left( \frac{19}{29} \right)
     \]
   - Simplifying the multiplication:
     \[
     \left( \frac{19}{2} \right) \times \left( \frac{19}{29} \right) = \frac{19 \times 19}{2 \times 29} = \frac{361}{58}
     \]
   - Simplifying the fraction:
     \[
     \frac{361}{58} = \frac{361 \div 29}{58 \div 29} = \frac{12.4483}{2} = 6.2241
     \]
   - Therefore, the vineyard produced approximately 6.2241 baskets of grapes this season.

2. **Calculating the number of baskets Jake gets to keep:**
   - Jake gets to keep \( \frac{7}{11} \) of the total amount of grapes.
   - To find the number of baskets Jake gets, we multiply the total baskets produced by \( \frac{7}{11} \):
     \[
     \text{Baskets Jake gets} = 6.2241 \times \frac{7}{11}
     \]
   - Simplifying the multiplication:
     \[
     6.2241 \times \frac{7}{11} = 6.2241 \times 0.6364 = 3.961
     \]
   - Therefore, Jake gets approximately 3.961 baskets of grapes.

3. **Calculating the number of baskets Jake uses for grape juice:**
   - Jake uses \( \frac{9}{10} \) of his grapes to make juice.
   - To find the number of baskets Jake uses for juice, we multiply the number of baskets he gets by \( \frac{9}{10} \):
     \[
     \text{Baskets used for juice} = 3.961 \times \frac{9}{10}
     \]
   - Simplifying the multiplication:
     \[
     3.961 \times \frac{9}{10} = 3.961 \times 0.9 = 3.5649
     \]
   - Therefore, Jake uses approximately 3.5649 baskets of grapes to make juice.

### Answer: 3.5649

Expected answer: 22743/6380

Correct? No

Problem: Joel has a grape farm. One day, he picked 9/2 bushels of red grapes and 10/22 bushels of green grapes from his farm. Calculate the total number of bushels of grapes Joel picked that day.

GPT-4o: 

To find the total number of bushels of grapes Joel picked, we need to add the bushels of red grapes and green grapes together.

First, let's convert the fractions to a common denominator if necessary. However, in this case, we can directly add the fractions since they are already in a simple form.

The red grapes picked are:
\[ \frac{9}{2} \]

The green grapes picked are:
\[ \frac{10}{22} \]

\[ \frac{10 \div 2}{22 \div 2} = \frac{5}{11} \]

Now, we need to add \(\frac{9}{2}\) and \(\frac{5}{11}\). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 2 and 11 is 22.

Convert \(\frac{9}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 22:
\[ \frac{9}{2} = \frac{9 \times 11}{2 \times 11} = \frac{99}{22} \]

Now we can add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{99}{22} + \frac{5}{11} = \frac{99}{22} + \frac{5 \times 2}{11 \times 2} = \frac{99}{22} + \frac{10}{22} = \frac{99 + 10}{22} = \frac{109}{22} \]

So, the total number of bushels of grapes Joel picked that day is:
\[ \frac{109}{22} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{109}{22}\)

Expected answer: 109/22

Correct? Yes

Problem: A snowman is constructed by stacking two different sized snowballs on top of each other. The larger snowball at the bottom has a diameter of 17/8 feet, and the smaller snowball on top has a diameter of 1/20 feet. What is the total height of the snowman in feet when these two snowballs are stacked on top of each other?

GPT-4o: 

To find the total height of the snowman, we need to add the diameters of the two snowballs.

First, let's convert the diameters to a common fraction format for easier addition:

1. The diameter of the larger snowball is \( \frac{17}{8} \) feet.
2. The diameter of the smaller snowball is \( \frac{1}{20} \) feet.

Next, we need to find a common denominator to add these fractions. The least common multiple (LCM) of 8 and 20 is 40.

Convert \( \frac{17}{8} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 40:
\[ \frac{17}{8} = \frac{17 \times 5}{8 \times 5} = \frac{85}{40} \]

Convert \( \frac{1}{20} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 40:
\[ \frac{1}{20} = \frac{1 \times 2}{20 \times 2} = \frac{2}{40} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{85}{40} + \frac{2}{40} = \frac{85 + 2}{40} = \frac{87}{40} \]

Thus, the total height of the snowman is \( \frac{87}{40} \) feet.

To convert this to a mixed number:
\[ \frac{87}{40} = 2 \frac{7}{40} \]

### Answer: \( 2 \frac{7}{40} \) feet

Problem: In a sandbox, a child splits up 24/7 parts of the sand in a fair way. Later on, another child takes away 2/16 part of the sand. Calculate the remaining part of sand in the sandbox.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's simplify the fractions involved.

The initial amount of sand is \( \frac{24}{7} \).

The amount of sand taken away is \( \frac{2}{16} \). Simplifying \( \frac{2}{16} \):
\[ \frac{2}{16} = \frac{1}{8} \]

Now, we need to subtract \( \frac{1}{8} \) from \( \frac{24}{7} \).

To perform this subtraction, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 7 and 8 is 56.

Convert \( \frac{24}{7} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 56:
\[ \frac{24}{7} = \frac{24 \times 8}{7 \times 8} = \frac{192}{56} \]

Convert \( \frac{1}{8} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 56:
\[ \frac{1}{8} = \frac{1 \times 7}{8 \times 7} = \frac{7}{56} \]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[ \frac{192}{56} - \frac{7}{56} = \frac{192 - 7}{56} = \frac{185}{56} \]

Thus, the remaining part of the sand in the sandbox is \( \frac{185}{56} \).

Problem: In the jungle, a lion ate 28/26 of a zebra in one day and 23/9 of a wildebeest the next day. How much less of the zebra did the lion eat compared with the wildebeest? Calculate your answer as a simplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much less of the zebra the lion ate compared to the wildebeest, we need to subtract the fraction of the zebra eaten from the fraction of the wildebeest eaten.

First, let's write down the fractions:
- Zebra: \( \frac{28}{26} \)
- Wildebeest: \( \frac{23}{9} \)

We need to subtract \( \frac{28}{26} \) from \( \frac{23}{9} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 26 and 9 is 234.

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 234:
- For the zebra: 
  \[
  \frac{28}{26} = \frac{28 \times 9}{26 \times 9} = \frac{252}{234}
  \]
- For the wildebeest:
  \[
  \frac{23}{9} = \frac{23 \times 26}{9 \times 26} = \frac{598}{234}
  \]

Now, subtract the fractions:
\[
\frac{598}{234} - \frac{252}{234} = \frac{598 - 252}{234} = \frac{346}{234}
\]

Simplify the fraction \( \frac{346}{234} \):
- The greatest common divisor (GCD) of 346 and 234 is 2.
- Divide both the numerator and the denominator by 2:
  \[
  \frac{346 \div 2}{234 \div 2} = \frac{173}{117}
  \]

Thus, the simplified fraction is \( \frac{173}{117} \).

### Answer: \(\frac{173}{117}\)

Expected answer: 173/117

Correct? Yes

\]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: In a beautiful forest, the park rangers recorded that 9 out of every 14 trees were pine trees. They also noticed an exceptional occurrence where 19 out of every 2 trees were birches. If you count all the pine trees and birch trees together, what fraction of the trees in the forest are either pine or birch? Use the formula f = ((9 / 14) + (19 / 2)) to solve this.

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem, we need to calculate the fraction of the trees that are either pine or birch using the given formula \( f = \left(\frac{9}{14}\right) + \left(\frac{19}{2}\right) \).

First, let's convert the fractions to have a common denominator. The least common multiple of 14 and 2 is 14.

1. Convert \(\frac{19}{2}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 14:
   \[
   \frac{19}{2} = \frac{19 \times 7}{2 \times 7} = \frac{133}{14}
   \]

2. Now, add the two fractions:
   \[
   \frac{9}{14} + \frac{133}{14} = \frac{9 + 133}{14} = \frac{142}{14}
   \]

3. Simplify the fraction:
   \[
   \frac{142}{14} = \frac{142 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{71}{7}
   \]

Thus, the fraction of the trees in the forest that are either pine or birch is \(\frac{71}{7}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{71}{7}\)

Expected answer: 71/7

Correct? Yes

   \]

Thus, the fraction of the trees in the forest that are either pine or birch is \(\frac{219}{14}\).

Expected answer: 219/14

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: On planet Zog, aliens use an interesting system to track their energy levels. At the beginning of the day, Zogorian calculates his energy level to be (14 / 2) / (23 / 17) zogs. Later in the day, after harnessing energy from their primary star, his energy level increases by (16 / 24) zogs. Calculate the Zogorian's energy level after the increase.

GPT-4o: 

First, we need to calculate the initial energy level of the Zogorian.

The initial energy level is given by:
\[
\frac{\left(\frac{14}{2}\right)}{\left(\frac{23}{17}\right)}
\]

First, simplify the numerator and the denominator separately:
\[
\frac{14}{2} = 7
\]
\[
\frac{23}{17} \text{ remains as it is.}
\]

Now, the expression becomes:
\[
\frac{7}{\frac{23}{17}}
\]

To divide by a fraction, multiply by its reciprocal:
\[
\frac{7}{\frac{23}{17}} = 7 \times \frac{17}{23} = \frac{7 \times 17}{23} = \frac{119}{23}
\]

Next, we need to add the increase in energy level, which is:
\[
\frac{16}{24}
\]

Simplify \(\frac{16}{24}\):
\[
\frac{16}{24} = \frac{2 \times 8}{3 \times 8} = \frac{2}{3}
\]

Now, add this to the initial energy level:
\[
\frac{119}{23} + \frac{2}{3}
\]

To add these fractions, find a common denominator. The least common multiple of 23 and 3 is 69:
\[
\frac{119}{23} = \frac{119 \times 3}{23 \times 3} = \frac{357}{69}
\]
\[
\frac{2}{3} = \frac{2 \times 23}{3 \times 23} = \frac{46}{69}
\]

Now, add the fractions:
\[
\frac{357}{69} + \frac{46}{69} = \frac{357 + 46}{69} = \frac{403}{69}
\]

Thus, the Zogorian's energy level after the increase is:
\[
\frac{403}{69}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{403}{69}\)

Expected answer: 403/69

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: After the Zogorian's energy level increased, he used a special device that multiplies the current energy level by a factor of (18 / 11) to store the additional energy for later use. Calculate the Zogorian's new energy level in zogs after using the device.

GPT-4o: 

To find the Zogorian's new energy level after using the device, we need to multiply the current energy level by the given factor.

The current energy level is:
\[
\frac{403}{69}
\]

The factor by which the energy level is multiplied is:
\[
\frac{18}{11}
\]

Now, multiply these two fractions:
\[
\frac{403}{69} \times \frac{18}{11}
\]

Multiply the numerators and the denominators:
\[
\frac{403 \times 18}{69 \times 11}
\]

Calculate the products:
\[
403 \times 18 = 7254
\]
\[
69 \times 11 = 759
\]

So, the new energy level is:
\[
\frac{7254}{759}
\]

To simplify this fraction, we need to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 7254 and 759. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(7254 \div 759 \approx 9.55\), so the integer part is 9.
2. \(7254 - 759 \times 9 = 7254 - 6831 = 423\)
3. \(759 \div 423 \approx 1.79\), so the integer part is 1.
4. \(759 - 423 = 336\)
5. \(423 \div 336 \approx 1.26\), so the integer part is 1.
6. \(423 - 336 = 87\)
7. \(336 \div 87 \approx 3.86\), so the integer part is 3.
8. \(336 - 87 \times 3 = 336 - 261 = 75\)
9. \(87 \div 75 \approx 1.16\), so the integer part is 1.
10. \(87 - 75 = 12\)
11. \(75 \div 12 \approx 6.25\), so the integer part is 6.
12. \(75 - 12 \times 6 = 75 - 72 = 3\)
13. \(12 \div 3 = 4\), so the integer part is 4.
14. \(12 - 3 \times 4 = 0\)

The GCD is 3. Now, divide both the numerator and the denominator by 3:
\[
\frac{7254 \div 3}{759 \div 3} = \frac{2418}{253}
\]

Thus, the Zogorian's new energy level is:
\[
\frac{2418}{253}
\]

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Teddy, the bear, loves to play hide and seek with his friends. One day, he decided to play a game where he hides some number of his stuffed animal friends. Teddy hides 18/11 of his friends in the forest and 8/21 of his friends at the beach. First calculate how many more friends Teddy hides in the forest than at the beach. Let's call this number 'f'. Then square 'f' to find 'n', the total number of hiding spots Teddy needs. How many hiding spots does Teddy need?

GPT-4o: 

To find how many more friends Teddy hides in the forest than at the beach, we need to subtract the fraction of friends hidden at the beach from the fraction hidden in the forest.

First, let's find a common denominator for the fractions \(\frac{18}{11}\) and \(\frac{8}{21}\). The least common multiple of 11 and 21 is 231.

Convert \(\frac{18}{11}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 231:
\[
\frac{18}{11} = \frac{18 \times 21}{11 \times 21} = \frac{378}{231}
\]

Convert \(\frac{8}{21}\) to a fraction with a denominator of 231:
\[
\frac{8}{21} = \frac{8 \times 11}{21 \times 11} = \frac{88}{231}
\]

Now, subtract the two fractions:
\[
\frac{378}{231} - \frac{88}{231} = \frac{378 - 88}{231} = \frac{290}{231}
\]

So, the number of friends Teddy hides more in the forest than at the beach is \(\frac{290}{231}\).

Next, we need to square this number to find the total number of hiding spots, \(n\):
\[
\left(\frac{290}{231}\right)^2 = \frac{290^2}{231^2} = \frac{84100}{53361}
\]

Thus, the total number of hiding spots Teddy needs is \(\frac{84100}{53361}\).

### Answer: \(\frac{84100}{53361}\)

Expected answer: 84100/53361

Correct? Yes

Problem: During rainy weather, a small snail moves at a snail-pace covering 17/21 of a meter in an hour. Another slightly faster snail covers 20/24 of a meter in the same time during such weather. One rainy day, the first snail started an hour earlier than the second. At the time when the second snail began, a third snail that covers 18/17 of a meter per hour also started moving. What is their total distance in meters 1 hour after all three have started moving? Compute the result using the operation ((17 / 21) + (20 / 24)) for the first two snails' distance, and multiply this result by (18 / 17) for the total distance , including the third snail.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to calculate the distance covered by each snail and then sum these distances.

First, let's simplify the distances covered by the first two snails in one hour.

1. The first snail covers \( \frac{17}{21} \) meters in one hour.
2. The second snail covers \( \frac{20}{24} \) meters in one hour. Simplifying \( \frac{20}{24} \):
   \[
   \frac{20}{24} = \frac{5}{6}
   \]

Now, we add the distances covered by the first two snails:
\[
\frac{17}{21} + \frac{5}{6}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 21 and 6 is 42.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 42:
\[
\frac{17}{21} = \frac{17 \times 2}{21 \times 2} = \frac{34}{42}
\]
\[
\frac{5}{6} = \frac{5 \times 7}{6 \times 7} = \frac{35}{42}
\]

Now add the fractions:
\[
\frac{34}{42} + \frac{35}{42} = \frac{34 + 35}{42} = \frac{69}{42}
\]

Next, we need to consider the third snail, which covers \( \frac{18}{17} \) meters in one hour.

The total distance covered by all three snails in one hour is:
\[
\left( \frac{69}{42} \right) + \left( \frac{18}{17} \right)
\]

To find the total distance, we need to add these two fractions. First, we need a common denominator for \( \frac{69}{42} \) and \( \frac{18}{17} \). The least common multiple of 42 and 17 is 714.

Convert each fraction to have a denominator of 714:
\[
\frac{69}{42} = \frac{69 \times 17}{42 \times 17} = \frac{1173}{714}
\]
\[
\frac{18}{17} = \frac{18 \times 42}{17 \times 42} = \frac{756}{714}
\]

Now add the fractions:
\[
\frac{1173}{714} + \frac{756}{714} = \frac{1173 + 756}{714} = \frac{1929}{714}
\]

Simplify the fraction:
\[
\frac{1929}{714} = \frac{1929 \div 3}{714 \div 3} = \frac{643}{238}
\]

Now add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{80}{105} + \frac{63}{105} = \frac{80 + 63}{105} = \frac{143}{105} \]

GPT-4o: 

To determine how much of the pile the monkey has left, we need to calculate the fractions of the pile that the monkey ate and gave away, and then subtract these from the whole pile.

First, let's calculate the fraction of the pile the monkey ate:
\[
\frac{22}{7} \times \frac{10}{25}
\]

We can simplify this multiplication by simplifying the fractions first:
\[
\frac{22}{7} \times \frac{10}{25} = \frac{22 \times 10}{7 \times 25} = \frac{220}{175}
\]

Next, we simplify \(\frac{220}{175}\):
\[
\frac{220}{175} = \frac{220 \div 5}{175 \div 5} = \frac{44}{35}
\]

So, the monkey ate \(\frac{44}{35}\) of the pile.

Next, let's calculate the fraction of the pile the monkey gave to his friend:
\[
\frac{3}{28}
\]

Now, we need to find the total fraction of the pile that the monkey has given away:
\[
\frac{44}{35} + \frac{3}{28}
\]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 35 and 28 is 140. We convert each fraction to have this common denominator:
\[
\frac{44}{35} = \frac{44 \times 4}{35 \times 4} = \frac{176}{140}
\]
\[
\frac{3}{28} = \frac{3 \times 5}{28 \times 5} = \frac{15}{140}
\]

Now, we add the fractions:
\[
\frac{176}{140} + \frac{15}{140} = \frac{176 + 15}{140} = \frac{191}{140}
\]

This is the total fraction of the pile that the monkey has eaten and given away. To find out how much of the pile the monkey has left, we subtract this from the whole pile (which is 1):
\[
1 - \frac{191}{140}
\]

We convert 1 to a fraction with the same denominator:
\[
1 = \frac{140}{140}
\]

Now, we perform the subtraction:
\[
\frac{140}{140} - \frac{191}{140} = \frac{140 - 191}{140} = \frac{-51}{140}
\]

Since a negative fraction doesn't make sense in this context, it indicates that the monkey has eaten and given away more than the whole pile, which suggests an error in the problem setup or interpretation. Problem: You decide to start a toothbrush collection and you add 7/15 of a new set of toothbrushes to your current collection. Suddenly, a friend gifts you 9 more sets. After grouping everything, you realized you can only fit 26/27 of them in your display case. How many sets of toothbrushes can you fit in your display case?

GPT-4o: 

Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. **Initial Addition to Collection:**
   You add \( \frac{7}{15} \) of a new set of toothbrushes to your current collection.

2. **Gift from Friend:**
   Your friend gifts you 9 more sets of toothbrushes.

3. **Total Sets Before Display Case Limitation:**
   The total number of sets you have is:
   \[
   \frac{7}{15} + 9
   \]
   To add these, we need a common denominator. The fraction \( \frac{7}{15} \) can be converted to a fraction with a denominator of 15:
   \[
   9 = \frac{135}{15}
   \]
   So, adding these together:
   \[
   \frac{7}{15} + \frac{135}{15} = \frac{142}{15}
   \]

4. **Fitting in the Display Case:**
   You can fit \( \frac{26}{27} \) of the total sets in your display case. Therefore, the number of sets you can fit is:
   \[
   \frac{26}{27} \times \frac{142}{15}
   \]
   Multiply the numerators and the denominators:
   \[
   \frac{26 \times 142}{27 \times 15} = \frac{3692}{405}
   \]

5. **Simplifying the Fraction:**
   To simplify \( \frac{3692}{405} \), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 3692 and 405. The GCD is 1, so the fraction is already in its simplest form.

6. **Converting to a Mixed Number:**
   Divide 3692 by 405:
   \[
   3692 \div 405 \approx 9.11
   \]
   Since we are dealing with sets of toothbrushes, we consider the integer part of the division:
   \[
   9 \text{ sets}
   \]

### Answer: 9

Expected answer: 3692/405

Correct? No

Finally, when considering his fuel efficiency rated at 22/15 nautical miles per gallon, Captain Alf multiplies his adjusted distance by this rate to figure out his fuel requirements. GPT-4o:

   - Distance to the island: \( \frac{17}{2} \) nautical miles
   - Current distance from the island: \( \frac{4}{2} \) nautical miles

   \[

Convert \( \frac{20}{21} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 609:
\[ \frac{20}{21} = \frac{20 \times 29}{21 \times 29} = \frac{580}{609} \]

Convert \( \frac{11}{29} \) to a fraction with a denominator of 609:
\[ \frac{11}{29} = \frac{11 \times 21}{29 \times 21} = \frac{231}{609} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{580}{609} + \frac{231}{609} = \frac{580 + 231}{609} = \frac{811}{609} \]

Thus, Arthur spends \( \frac{811}{609} \) hours practicing the piano each day on the weekend.

### Answer: \( \frac{811}{609} \) hours

Expected answer: 811/609

Correct? Yes

How many more or fewer shirts does each sibling now have as compared to before? Calculate the difference using the expression ((18 / 3) - (27 / 19)) and find out the result.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's determine how many shirts each sibling initially received. Lucas had 18 shirts and divided them equally among his 3 siblings:

\[
\frac{18}{3} = 6
\]

So, each sibling initially received 6 shirts.

Next, Lucas bought 27 more shirts and decided to keep only \(\frac{1}{19}\) of those shirts for each sibling. We need to calculate how many shirts each sibling received from the new batch:

\[
\frac{27}{19}
\]

Now, we need to find the difference in the number of shirts each sibling has now compared to before. This is given by the expression:

\[
\left( \frac{18}{3} \right) - \left( \frac{27}{19} \right)
\]

Substituting the values we calculated:

\[
6 - \frac{27}{19}
\]

To perform this subtraction, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 6 and \(\frac{27}{19}\) is 19. We convert 6 to a fraction with a denominator of 19:

\[
6 = \frac{6 \times 19}{19} = \frac{114}{19}
\]

Now, we subtract the fractions:

\[

Finally, we simplify \(\frac{87}{19}\):

\[
\frac{87}{19} = 4.578947368421053

So, each sibling now has approximately 4.58 fewer shirts compared to before.

Problem: Callie owns a pen business. Last month, she sold 20 pens for every 15 she produced. At the same time, she sold an additional 16 pens for every 22 she put out for sale. Meanwhile, she found that for every 22 pens she advertised, 27 were interested customers. For each 23 pens she produced this week, she was able to sell 8. What is the result when she multiplies the ratio of last month's sales to production (20/15 + 16/22) and this week's figure for the ratio of interested customers to production (22/27 * 23/8)? Leave your answer as an unsimplified fraction.

GPT-4o: 

To solve this problem, we need to calculate two ratios and then multiply them together.

First, let's find the ratio of last month's sales to production. This ratio is given by the sum of two fractions:
\[ \frac{20}{15} + \frac{16}{22} \]

We can simplify each fraction individually:
\[ \frac{20}{15} = \frac{4}{3} \]
\[ \frac{16}{22} = \frac{8}{11} \]

Now, we need to add these two fractions. To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 3 and 11 is 33:
\[ \frac{4}{3} = \frac{4 \times 11}{3 \times 11} = \frac{44}{33} \]
\[ \frac{8}{11} = \frac{8 \times 3}{11 \times 3} = \frac{24}{33} \]

Adding these fractions together:
\[ \frac{44}{33} + \frac{24}{33} = \frac{44 + 24}{33} = \frac{68}{33} \]

Next, let's find the ratio of interested customers to production for this week:
\[ \frac{22}{27} \times \frac{23}{8} \]

We multiply these fractions directly:
\[ \frac{22 \times 23}{27 \times 8} = \frac{506}{216} \]

Now, we multiply the two results together:
\[ \frac{68}{33} \times \frac{506}{216} = \frac{68 \times 506}{33 \times 216} = \frac{34408}{7128} \]

Thus, the result when she multiplies the ratio of last month's sales to production and this week's figure for the ratio of interested customers to production is:
### Answer: \(\frac{34408}{7128}\)

Expected answer: 391/81

Correct? Yes

Problem: Consider a band practice session in which a musician played a song for exactly 30 minutes. After dividing this time equally between 15 songs, how much time did they spend on each song? From this average time per song, the band reduced the time spent on a particular song by 1/17 of an hour. Can you calculate the final duration of that song?

GPT-4o: 

First, we need to determine the time spent on each song during the practice session. The total time spent is 30 minutes, and this time is divided equally among 15 songs.

To find the time spent on each song, we divide the total time by the number of songs:
\[
\text{Time per song} = \frac{30 \text{ minutes}}{15 \text{ songs}} = 2 \text{ minutes per song}
\]

Next, we need to convert the time per song into hours since the reduction is given in hours. There are 60 minutes in an hour, so:
\[
2 \text{ minutes} = \frac{2}{60} \text{ hours} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ hours}
\]

The band reduced the time spent on a particular song by \(\frac{1}{17}\) of an hour. We need to subtract this reduction from the original time per song:
\[
\text{Final duration} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ hours} - \frac{1}{17} \text{ hours}
\]

To perform this subtraction, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 30 and 17 is 510. We convert both fractions to have this common denominator:
\[
\frac{1}{30} = \frac{17}{510}
\]
\[
\frac{1}{17} = \frac{30}{510}
\]

Now we subtract the fractions:
\[
\frac{17}{510} - \frac{30}{510} = \frac{17 - 30}{510} = \frac{-13}{510} = -\frac{13}{510}
\]

Since we are dealing with time, we should consider the absolute value:
\[
\left| -\frac{13}{510} \right| = \frac{13}{510}
\]

Simplifying \(\frac{13}{510}\):
\[
\frac{13}{510} = \frac{1}{39.23} \approx 0.0255 \text{ hours}
\]

Converting this back to minutes:
\[
0.0255 \text{ hours} \times 60 \text{ minutes/hour} \approx 1.53 \text{ minutes}
\]

### Answer: 1.53 minutes

Expected answer: 33/17

Correct? No

Problem: Josh rented a scooter for a day. He rode the scooter for a total of 18 hours during the first day. The next day, he rode the scooter for an additional 1/12 of an hour. Later that afternoon, his friend Jack also rented a scooter and rode it for 7/17 of an hour. How many hours did they both ride scooters in total (expressed as a fraction)? Combine the hours they both rode and simplify the fraction to get the answer.

GPT-4o: 

First, let's convert the hours Josh rode the scooter into a fraction. Josh rode the scooter for 18 hours and an additional \( \frac{1}{12} \) of an hour. 

To combine these, we need to express 18 as a fraction with a common denominator of 12:
\[ 18 = \frac{18 \times 12}{12} = \frac{216}{12} \]

Adding the additional \( \frac{1}{12} \) hour:
\[ \frac{216}{12} + \frac{1}{12} = \frac{216 + 1}{12} = \frac{217}{12} \]

Next, we consider the time Jack rode the scooter, which is \( \frac{7}{17} \) of an hour.

To find the total time both Josh and Jack rode the scooters, we need to add \( \frac{217}{12} \) and \( \frac{7}{17} \). To do this, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 12 and 17 is 204.

\[ \frac{217}{12} = \frac{217 \times 17}{12 \times 17} = \frac{3689}{204} \]
\[ \frac{7}{17} = \frac{7 \times 12}{17 \times 12} = \frac{84}{204} \]

Now, add the two fractions:
\[ \frac{3689}{204} + \frac{84}{204} = \frac{3689 + 84}{204} = \frac{3773}{204} \]

The fraction \( \frac{3773}{204} \) is already in its simplest form because 3773 and 204 have no common factors other than 1.

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple (LCM) of 19 and 11 is 209.

Convert each fraction to have the common denominator of 209:
\[ \frac{26}{19} = \frac{26 \times 11}{19 \times 11} = \frac{286}{209} \]
\[ \frac{7}{11} = \frac{7 \times 19}{11 \times 19} = \frac{133}{209} \]

Now, add the fractions:
\[ \frac{286}{209} + \frac{133}{209} = \frac{286 + 133}{209} = \frac{419}{209} \]

Next, Oliver decides to use \(\frac{26}{8}\) of this combined string. We need to multiply \(\frac{419}{209}\) by \(\frac{26}{8}\):
\[ \frac{419}{209} \times \frac{26}{8} = \frac{419 \times 26}{209 \times 8} = \frac{10894}{1672} \]

Thus, the length of the kite string that Oliver is using now is:

Solve the following equations to find the variable 'j': u = 9/19 + 6/8 j = u + 4/1

GPT-4o: 

To solve the problem, we need to find the total number of snowballs Mike had after finding more. We will solve the given equations step by step.

First, let's solve for \( u \):

\[ u = \frac{9}{19} + \frac{6}{8} \]

To add these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 19 and 8 is 152.

\[ \frac{9}{19} = \frac{9 \times 8}{19 \times 8} = \frac{72}{152} \]
\[ \frac{6}{8} = \frac{6 \times 19}{8 \times 19} = \frac{114}{152} \]

\[ u = \frac{72}{152} + \frac{114}{152} = \frac{72 + 114}{152} = \frac{186}{152} \]

Simplify the fraction:

\[ \frac{186}{152} = \frac{93}{76} \]

So, \( u = \frac{93}{76} \).

\[ j = u + \frac{4}{1} \]

\[ j = \frac{93}{76} + \frac{4}{1} \]

Convert \( \frac{4}{1} \) to have a denominator of 76:

Now add the fractions:

\[ j = \frac{93}{76} + \frac{304}{76} = \frac{93 + 304}{76} = \frac{397}{76} \]

So, the total number of snowballs Mike had after finding more is:

Problem: In a chocolate factory, one worker packages 26 pieces of chocolate in 18 minutes, while another worker can package 15 pieces of chocolate every 15 minutes. Find out the total amount of chocolate they can package in one minute.

GPT-4o: 

To determine the total amount of chocolate both workers can package in one minute, we need to find their individual rates and then sum them up.

First, let's find the rate for the first worker:
- The first worker packages 26 pieces of chocolate in 18 minutes.
- The rate of the first worker is \( \frac{26 \text{ pieces}}{18 \text{ minutes}} \).

To find the rate per minute, we divide 26 by 18:
\[ \frac{26}{18} = \frac{13}{9} \text{ pieces per minute} \]

Next, let's find the rate for the second worker:
- The second worker packages 15 pieces of chocolate in 15 minutes.
- The rate of the second worker is \( \frac{15 \text{ pieces}}{15 \text{ minutes}} \).

To find the rate per minute, we divide 15 by 15:
\[ \frac{15}{15} = 1 \text{ piece per minute} \]

Now, we sum the rates of both workers to find the total amount of chocolate they can package in one minute:
\[ \frac{13}{9} + 1 = \frac{13}{9} + \frac{9}{9} = \frac{22}{9} \text{ pieces per minute} \]

### Answer: \(\frac{22}{9}\) pieces per minute

Expected answer: 22/9

Correct? Yes

Problem: Debra is baking cookies and she realizes she has two different recipes for the same type of cookie. She's wondering if she combines the ingredients from both, if she will end up with even more cookies or not. The first recipe requires (27 / 3) cups flour and (11 / 7) cups sugar. She determines the ratio of flour to sugar by dividing the amount of flour by the amount of sugar. She then subtracts (21 / 26) from this ratio because that's how many cups of sugar her friend says makes the cookies too sweet. After that, she adds (22 / 9) cups of flour from the second recipe to the new ratio to see how many total cups of flour she will need. How many cups of flour will she have in the end?

GPT-4o: 

Let's break down the problem step by step.

1. Calculate the amount of flour and sugar in the first recipe:
   - Flour: \( \frac{27}{3} = 9 \) cups
   - Sugar: \( \frac{11}{7} \) cups

2. Determine the ratio of flour to sugar:
   \[
   \text{Ratio} = \frac{\text{Flour}}{\text{Sugar}} = \frac{9}{\frac{11}{7}} = 9 \times \frac{7}{11} = \frac{63}{11}
   \]

3. Subtract \( \frac{21}{26} \) from this ratio:
   \[
   \frac{63}{11} - \frac{21}{26}
   \]

   To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 11 and 26 is 286.

   Convert each fraction to have the common denominator:
   \[
   \frac{63}{11} = \frac{63 \times 26}{11 \times 26} = \frac{1638}{286}
   \]
   \[
   \frac{21}{26} = \frac{21 \times 11}{26 \times 11} = \frac{231}{286}
   \]

   Now subtract the fractions:
   \[
   \frac{1638}{286} - \frac{231}{286} = \frac{1407}{286}
   \]

4. Simplify the fraction \( \frac{1407}{286} \):
   \[
   \frac{1407 \div 13}{286 \div 13} = \frac{108.23}{22} \approx 4.92
   \]

5. Add \( \frac{22}{9} \) cups of flour from the second recipe to the new ratio:
   \[
   4.92 + \frac{22}{9}
   \]

   Convert \( \frac{22}{9} \) to a decimal:
   \[
   \frac{22}{9} \approx 2.44
   \]

   Add the two values:
   \[
   4.92 + 2.44 = 7.36
   \]

### Answer: 7.36

Problem: There are 26/13 chickens in one farm and 9/16 chickens in another farm. Farmer John calculated the difference between the number of chickens in the two farms. After a week, the number of chickens multiplied by 19/21 due to new chickens born. How many chickens are there now in Farmer John's farm?

GPT-4o: 

First, let's calculate the number of chickens in each farm.

For the first farm:
\[
\frac{26}{13} = 2 \text{ chickens}
\]

For the second farm:
\[
\frac{9}{16} \text{ chickens}
\]

Next, we find the difference between the number of chickens in the two farms:
\[
2 - \frac{9}{16}
\]

To subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The common denominator for 2 (which is \(\frac{32}{16}\)) and \(\frac{9}{16}\) is 16:
\[
2 = \frac{32}{16}
\]

So, the difference is:
\[
\frac{32}{16} - \frac{9}{16} = \frac{23}{16} \text{ chickens}
\]

After a week, the number of chickens multiplied by \(\frac{19}{21}\):
\[
\frac{23}{16} \times \frac{19}{21} = \frac{23 \times 19}{16 \times 21} = \frac{437}{336}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{437}{336}\), we check for common factors. Since 437 and 336 have no common factors other than 1, the fraction is already in its simplest form.

### Answer: \(\frac{437}{336}\)

Expected answer: 437/336

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Problem

Problem: Professor Astro is working on his telescope. He believes the power of his telescope is directly proportional to the sum of two fractions. The first fraction is the light gathering power of the lens, which is 24 out of 27. The second fraction is the zooming potential, which is 30 out of 26. So, Professor Astro calculates the sum of these two fractions ((24 / 27) + (30 / 26)). What does he find?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the two fractions \(\frac{24}{27}\) and \(\frac{30}{26}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 27 and 26, and their least common multiple (LCM) is 27 * 26 = 702.

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

1. Convert \(\frac{24}{27}\):
\[
\frac{24}{27} = \frac{24 \times 26}{27 \times 26} = \frac{624}{702}
\]

2. Convert \(\frac{30}{26}\):
\[
\frac{30}{26} = \frac{30 \times 27}{26 \times 27} = \frac{810}{702}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{624}{702} + \frac{810}{702} = \frac{624 + 810}{702} = \frac{1434}{702}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{1434}{702}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1434 and 702. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(1434 \div 702 = 2\) with a remainder of \(1434 - 2 \times 702 = 30\)
2. \(702 \div 30 = 23\) with a remainder of \(702 - 23 \times 30 = 12\)
3. \(30 \div 12 = 2\) with a remainder of \(30 - 2 \times 12 = 6\)
4. \(12 \div 6 = 2\) with a remainder of \(12 - 2 \times 6 = 0\)

The GCD is 6. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 6:
\[
\frac{1434 \div 6}{702 \div 6} = \frac{239}{117}
\]

Thus, the simplified sum of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{239}{117}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{239}{117}\)

Expected answer: 239/117

Correct? Yes

ðŸ”— Follow-up

Problem: Upon recalculating his telescope's potential with more accurate data, Professor Astro realizes that the light gathering power of his lens is actually 12 out of 27, not 24 out of 27 as previously calculated. Professor Astro recalculates the sum of these two fractions ((12 / 27) + (30 / 26)). What is the resulting sum now?

GPT-4o: 

To find the sum of the two fractions \(\frac{12}{27}\) and \(\frac{30}{26}\), we first need to find a common denominator. The denominators are 27 and 26, and their least common multiple (LCM) is 27 * 26 = 702.

Next, we convert each fraction to have this common denominator:

1. Convert \(\frac{12}{27}\):
\[
\frac{12}{27} = \frac{12 \times 26}{27 \times 26} = \frac{312}{702}
\]

2. Convert \(\frac{30}{26}\):
\[
\frac{30}{26} = \frac{30 \times 27}{26 \times 27} = \frac{810}{702}
\]

Now, we add the two fractions:
\[
\frac{312}{702} + \frac{810}{702} = \frac{312 + 810}{702} = \frac{1122}{702}
\]

To simplify \(\frac{1122}{702}\), we find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of 1122 and 702. Using the Euclidean algorithm:

1. \(1122 \div 702 = 1\) with a remainder of \(1122 - 1 \times 702 = 420\)
2. \(702 \div 420 = 1\) with a remainder of \(702 - 1 \times 420 = 282\)
3. \(420 \div 282 = 1\) with a remainder of \(420 - 1 \times 282 = 138\)
4. \(282 \div 138 = 2\) with a remainder of \(282 - 2 \times 138 = 6\)
5. \(138 \div 6 = 23\) with a remainder of \(138 - 23 \times 6 = 0\)

The GCD is 6. We divide both the numerator and the denominator by 6:
\[
\frac{1122 \div 6}{702 \div 6} = \frac{187}{117}
\]

Thus, the simplified sum of the fractions is:
\[
\frac{187}{117}
\]

### Answer: \(\frac{187}{117}\)

Expected answer: 187/117

Correct? Yes

Problem: Jaden is a dairy farmer who milks his cows twice a day. In the morning, his cows give him 26/14 gallons of milk per cow, and in the evening, they give 28/20 gallons of milk per cow. If he multiplies these two fractions together, how much milk is he getting from one cow in one day?

GPT-4o: 

To find out how much milk Jaden gets from one cow in one day, we need to multiply the two fractions representing the morning and evening milk yields.

First, let's simplify the fractions if possible:
- The morning yield is \( \frac{26}{14} \). We can simplify this by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
  \[
  \frac{26}{14} = \frac{26 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{13}{7}
  \]

- The evening yield is \( \frac{28}{20} \). We can simplify this by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 4:
  \[
  \frac{28}{20} = \frac{28 \div 4}{20 \div 4} = \frac{7}{5}
  \]

Now, we multiply the simplified fractions:
\[
\frac{13}{7} \times \frac{7}{5}
\]

When multiplying fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{13 \times 7}{7 \times 5} = \frac{91}{35}
\]

Next, we simplify \( \frac{91}{35} \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 7:
\[
\frac{91}{35} = \frac{91 \div 7}{35 \div 7} = \frac{13}{5}
\]

Thus, Jaden gets \( \frac{13}{5} \) gallons of milk from one cow in one day.

### Answer: \(\frac{13}{5}\) gallons

Expected answer: 13/5

Correct? Yes

Problem: Following the previous problem, let's consider that Jaden has made some changes on his farm that affected the milk production in the evening. Now, his cows give him 28/10 gallons of milk per cow in the evening instead of the previous 28/20 gallons. If we still take the morning milk production as 26/14 gallons per cow, how much milk is he getting from one cow in one day now?

GPT-4o: 

To determine the new total amount of milk Jaden gets from one cow in one day, we need to multiply the morning and evening milk yields.

First, let's simplify the fractions if possible:
- The morning yield is \( \frac{26}{14} \). We can simplify this by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
  \[
  \frac{26}{14} = \frac{26 \div 2}{14 \div 2} = \frac{13}{7}
  \]

- The new evening yield is \( \frac{28}{10} \). We can simplify this by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 2:
  \[
  \frac{28}{10} = \frac{28 \div 2}{10 \div 2} = \frac{14}{5}
  \]

Now, we multiply the simplified fractions:
\[
\frac{13}{7} \times \frac{14}{5}
\]

When multiplying fractions, we multiply the numerators together and the denominators together:
\[
\frac{13 \times 14}{7 \times 5} = \frac{182}{35}
\]

Next, we simplify \( \frac{182}{35} \) by dividing both the numerator and the denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 7:
\[
\frac{182}{35} = \frac{182 \div 7}{35 \div 7} = \frac{26}{5}
\]

Thus, Jaden gets \( \frac{26}{5} \) gallons of milk from one cow in one day.

### Answer: \(\frac{26}{5}\) gallons

Expected answer: 26/5
